Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
The Five Negative Attributes of Allah
Sanusi enumerates the five negative attributes: qidam, baqa, qiyam bi nafsihi, mukhalafa, wahdaniyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five negative attributes (sifat salbiyya) that negate from Allah what is not befitting, and their significance in affirming Allah's transcendence.

Core Idea
Five negations protect Allah's transcendence: pre-eternity, permanence, self-subsistence, dissimilarity, and oneness.

This passage from al-Bahja al-Saniyya introduces the five negative attributes of Allah. These attributes are not positive descriptions but negations of imperfections. Understanding them is crucial for tawhid, as they safeguard the concept of Allah's absolute perfection and uniqueness.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic poem
Read the Arabic lines carefully, noticing the rhythm and the sequence of attributes. Then read the literal translation.
The poem is written in rajaz meter, a common teaching format.
2
Identify the five attributes
Locate each of the five negative attributes in the poem: qidam, baqa, qiyam bi nafsihi, mukhalafa, and wahdaniyya. Understand that they negate flaws from Allah.
The word 'salbiyya' means negative or privative.
3
Understand the concluding line
The final line states that effective causation (ta'thir) is only for Allah. Reflect on how this connects to the five attributes, especially wahdaniyya (oneness).
This line reinforces tawhid and rejects any other independent cause.
4
Reflect on the meaning of 'tilt al-tuqa'
The phrase 'these are piety' indicates that believing in these attributes is an act of piety. Consider why negating imperfections from Allah is a form of worship.
Piety (tuqa) here refers to safeguarding one's faith by affirming Allah's transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذِي تُسَمَّى صِفةٌ نَفْسِيَّةَ * ثُمَّ تَلِيهَا خَمْسَةُ سَلْبِيَّةُ * وَهْيَ القِدَمَ بِالذَّاتِ فَاعْلَمُ والبَقَا * قِيامُهُ بِنَفْسِهِ، تِلْتَ التَّقَى * مُخَالِفٌ للغَيْرِ، وَحْدَانِيَّةٌ * فِي الذَّاتِ، أَوْ صِفَاتِهِ العَلِيَّة * والفِعْلِ، فَالتَّأْثِيرُ لَيْسَ إِلَّا * لِلوَاحِدِ القَهَّارِ جَلَّ وعلا
And this is called a self-attribute (sifa nafsiyya), then it is followed by five negative ones (salbiyya): they are: pre-eternity (qidam) of the essence, so know; and permanence (baqa); self-subsistence (qiyamuhu bi nafsihi); these are piety; being different from others (mukhalif lil ghayr); and oneness (wahdaniyya) in essence, or in His high attributes, and in action. So effective causation (al-ta'thir) is only for the One, the All-Dominant, exalted and high.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage lists the five negative attributes (sifat salbiyya) that negate from Allah what is not befitting. First, it mentions that the attribute of existence is a 'sifa nafsiyya' (self-attribute). Then it lists five negative attributes: (1) qidam: pre-eternity; (2) baqa: permanence; (3) qiyam bi nafsihi: self-subsistence; (4) mukhalafa lil ghayr: dissimilarity to others; (5) wahdaniyya: oneness in essence, attributes, and actions. The line 'tilt al-tuqa' (these are piety) indicates that holding these beliefs is a form of piety. The passage concludes that effective causation (ta'thir) belongs only to Allah, the One, the All-Dominant.

Key Terms
صفة نفسية
صفات سلبية
القدم
البقاء
القيام بالنفس
مخالفة للغير
وحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the five negative attributes are separate entities added to Allah's essence.
Correction: The five negative attributes are pure negations; they do not imply multiplicity in Allah. They simply describe what Allah is not.

Checkpoint
How many negative attributes (sifat salbiyya) does the author list?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The five negative attributes protect Allah's transcendence by negating all imperfections, affirming His absolute oneness and sole causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel anxious about your future, do you truly believe that Allah is self-subsistent and needs no support, or do you act as if your security depends on other things? How can you internalize qiyam bi nafsihi so that it changes your trust in Allah alone?
?
The attribute of mukhalafa affirms that Allah is unlike anything. When you imagine Allah in your mind, do you ever unconsciously compare Him to something created? How will you actively purge such images from your thoughts?
?
Wahdaniyya in action means that only Allah creates and controls outcomes. In your daily efforts, do you attribute success or failure to your own skill or to others, forgetting that all effective causation is only for the One? How can you remind yourself of this throughout your day?

Divine Attributes

The Seven Attributes of Ma'ani
Sanusi lists the seven essential attributes of Allah: knowledge, life, power, will, speech, hearing, sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven essential attributes of Allah (the 'ma'ani') and the distinction between His will and His command.

Core Idea
Seven eternal attributes define Allah's essence; His will is not identical to His command.

Sanusi now turns from the general classification of attributes to the specific list of seven that are called 'attributes of ma'ani.' These are real, eternal qualities that subsist in Allah's essence. The passage also contains an important clarification: Allah's will (irada) is not the same as His command (amr), a distinction that avoids theological confusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic poem
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noting the names of the attributes as they appear in the poetic lines.
The poem uses rhyme and meter, so read it aloud if possible.
2
Identify the seven attributes
From the text, list the seven attributes of ma'ani: knowledge, life, power, will, speech, hearing, sight.
3
Understand the qasd-amr distinction
The line 'الْقَصْدُ غَيْرُ الأمرِ' tells us that purpose (qasd) is distinct from command (amr). This clarifies that Allah's will may not always correspond to what He commands.
This prevents confusion about divine decree and command.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The poem ends by affirming that Allah is al-fa'il (the Agent) and al-mukhtar (the Free Chooser), grounding the attributes in His active freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْمَعَانِي سَبْعَةُ للرَّائِي * أي عِلْمُهُ الْمُحِيطُ بالأَشْيَاءِ * حَياتُهُ وقُدْرَةٌ إرادة * وكُلُّ شيءٍ كَائِنْ أَرَادَة * وإنْ يَكُنْ بِضِدِّهِ قَدْ أَمَرا * فالقَصْدُ غيرُ الأمرِ فاطرَح المِرَا * فقَد عَلِمتَ أربَعًا أَقْسَامَا * فِي الكَائِنَاتِ فَاحْفَظِ الْمَقَامَا * كَلامُهُ والسَّمْعُ والإِبْصَارُ * فَهُوَ الإِلهُ الفَاعِلُ الْمُخْتَارُ
Then the attributes of ma'ani are seven for the seer: that is His knowledge encompassing all things, His life, power, will, and everything that is He wills. And if He has commanded (amara) something contrary to it (i.e., contrary to His will?), then purpose (al-qasd) is other than command (al-amr), so cast aside dispute. For you have known four divisions in the existent things, so preserve the station. His speech, hearing, and sight – so He is the God, the Agent, the Free Choiser.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage enumerates the seven attributes of ma'ani (meaningful attributes) that are eternally predicated of Allah. The author says there are seven for the one who reflects (al-ra'i). They are: (1) knowledge ('ilm) encompassing all things, (2) life (hayat), (3) power (qudra), (4) will (irada), (5) speech (kalam), (6) hearing (sam'), (7) sight (basar). The passage includes a parenthetical note: 'And if He has commanded (amara) something contrary to it (i.e., contrary to His will?), then purpose (qasd) is not the same as command, so avoid argument.' This likely distinguishes between God's will (irada) and His command (amr), clarifying that what He wills may not be what He commands (e.g., He wills the existence of disbelievers but does not command their disbelief). The author then says you have known four divisions in the existent things – possibly referring to the earlier classification of the world into four categories? Then he lists speech, hearing, and sight, concluding that Allah is the agent (al-fa'il) and the free chooser (al-mukhtar).

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
العلم
الحياة
القدرة
الإرادة
الكلام
السمع
البصر
القصد
الأمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These seven attributes are parts or components of Allah.
Correction: They are eternal aspects of His essence, not parts. They are not separable from Him.

Checkpoint
How many attributes of ma'ani are mentioned?
A) Five
B) Seven
C) Eight
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The seven attributes of ma'ani (knowledge, life, power, will, speech, hearing, sight) are eternal and inherent to Allah, and His will is distinct from His command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or a sin you committed, do you truly believe that it occurred by Allah's will? Or do you secretly resent that His command (what He wants you to do) seems different from what He willed? Tonight, before you sleep, identify one specific situation where you have struggled to accept His will, and say 'I submit to Your will even if I do not understand it.'
?
You have learned that Allah has seven attributes. Which of these attributes do you most need to be reminded of in your daily life? For instance, how would remembering His all-encompassing knowledge change how you speak or act when you are alone? Make a concrete plan to reflect on one attribute each day this week.
?
The poem ends by calling Allah 'al-Fa'il al-Mukhtar'—the Agent, the Free Chooser. Do you live as if you are the one in control, or do you actively surrender your choices to Him? What is one decision you are facing right now where you need to recognize His free choice over yours? Will you make a dua tonight asking Him to align your will with His?

Divine Attributes
beginner

The Self-Attribute and the Five Negative Attributes
Enumeration of the nafsiyya attribute and five salbiyya attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the self-attribute (nafsiyya) and be able to list and explain the five negative attributes of Allah.

Core Idea
The self-attribute is Allah's existence itself; the five negative attributes negate all imperfection.

In this passage, the author introduces the concept of the self-attribute (ṣifa nafsiyya), which is simply Allah's necessary existence. He then enumerates five negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyya) that negate any possible imperfection from Allah. Understanding these categories is foundational for Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic poetic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the content.
The verse structure uses rhyme for memorization.
2
Identify the self-attribute argument
Find the part where the author states that existence (wujūd) is a necessary attribute of Allah and note the causal proof given.
The proof uses the principle that every effect points to a cause.
3
List the five negative attributes
Identify each of the five negative attributes as they appear: eternal, everlasting, self-subsistence, different from others, oneness.
These are called 'negative' because they deny imperfections.
4
Reflect on why these are called 'negative'
Consider how each attribute negates a potential deficiency in Allah, reinforcing His perfection and uniqueness.
They are not positive attributes added to the essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاعْلَمْ بأنَّ الوَصْفَ بالوُجُودِ * مِنْ وَاجِبَاتِ الْوَاحِدِ الْمَعْبُودِ إِذْ ظَاهِرُ بأنَّ كُلَّ أَثَرِ * يَهْدِي إِلَى مُؤثِرٍ فَاعْتَبِرِ وذِي تُسَمَّى صِفةٌ نَفْسِيَّةَ . ثُمَّ تَلِيهَا خَمْسَةُ سَلْبِيَّةُ وَهْيَ القِدَمَ بِالذَّاتِ فَاعْلَمُ والبَقَا * قِيامُهُ بِنَفْسِهِ، تِلْتَ التَّقَى مُخَالِفٌ للغَيْرِ، وَحْدَانِيَّةٌ * فِي الذَّاتِ، أَوْ صِفَاتِهِ العَلِيَّة
Know that the attribute of existence is among the necessities of the One who is worshipped. For it is clear that every effect guides to an efficient cause, so reflect. And this is called the self-attribute. Then come five negative attributes after it: eternal in essence, and know, and everlasting, self-subsistence, that is the path of piety, different from others, oneness in essence or His high attributes.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage defines the self-attribute (ṣifa nafsiyya) and the five negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyya). First, the author states that existence (wujūd) is a necessary attribute of God—it is not derived but self-evident. He then provides a causal argument: every effect points to a cause (which is God). Then he introduces the self-attribute (essence) and lists the five negative attributes: qidam (eternality), baqā' (everlastingness), qiyām bi nafsih (self-subsistence), mukhālafa lil-ghayr (difference from creation), and waḥdāniyya (oneness). These are called 'negative' because they negate imperfection from God, affirming His uniqueness.

Key Terms
صفة نفسية
خمسة سلبية
الوجود
القدم
البقا
قيامه بنفسه
مخالف للغير
وحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The self-attribute is an additional attribute distinct from Allah's essence.
Correction: The self-attribute is the essence itself; it is not something added.

Checkpoint
How many negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyya) are listed after the self-attribute?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Allah's existence is a necessary self-attribute, and five negative attributes protect His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if Allah's existence is the most certain reality, or do your daily actions suggest you forget this self-evident truth? How can you make His existence more present in your heart today?
?
Which of the five negative attributes do you find hardest to internalize? For instance, do you ever subconsciously imagine Allah as being like something created? What step will you take to uproot that comparison from your heart?
?
If someone asked you why Allah cannot be limited by time, place, or multiplicity, could you answer from this passage? Commit to memorizing the five negative attributes and their meanings so you can defend God's transcendence when needed.

The Seven Attributes of Meaning Enumeration
Enumeration of the seven attributes of meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the list of the seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt ma'ānī) and that they are real, distinct attributes subsisting in the divine essence.

Core Idea
The seven attributes of meaning are real distinct perfections in God's essence.

This lesson presents the enumeration of the seven ‘attributes of meaning’ (ṣifāt ma'ānī) which are central to Ashʿarī theology. These attributes are not mere names but real qualities that subsist in the divine essence, as the author states they are seven: knowledge, life, power, will, and by implication hearing, sight, and speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic lines
Read the first two lines of the poem which state that the attributes of meaning are seven and list the first four: knowledge, life, power, will.
The phrase 'for the seer' indicates these are known through reflection.
2
Identify the seven
Note that only four are explicitly mentioned; the remaining three (hearing, sight, speech) are inferred from other passages of the same poem.
3
Understand 'attributes of meaning'
These are attributes that are additional to the essence and have a meaning (ma'nā) that subsists in the essence, causing it to be described by that attribute.
This distinguishes them from mere attributive expressions.
4
Reflect on the nature
Consider why the author emphasizes that these attributes are seven and that they are 'for the seer' meaning they are known through rational and revealed evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْمَعَانِي سَبْعَةُ للرَّائِي * أي عِلْمُهُ الْمُحِيطُ بِالأَشْيَاءِ حَياتُهُ وقُدْرَةٌ إرادة * وكُلُّ شيءٍ كَائِنْ أَرَادَة وإنْ يَكُنْ بِضِدِّهِ قَدْ أَمَرا * فالقَصْدُ غيرُ الأمرِ فاطرَح المِرَا
Then the attributes of meaning are seven for the seer: that is, His knowledge encompassing all things, His life, power, will. And everything that is happening is what He willed. And if He may have commanded its opposite, then intention is different from command, so abandon dispute.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage lists the seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt ma'ānī). The author states they are seven: knowledge ('ilm), life (ḥayāh), power (qudra), will (irāda), and by implication hearing, sight, and speech (from later lines). He emphasizes that God's knowledge encompasses all things, and everything that occurs is by His will (irāda). He also makes a distinction: God's command (amr) may sometimes be opposite to His will (e.g., He commands good but wills trial). Thus, 'intention' (qaṣd) is not identical to 'command'—this is a key Ashʿarī point to reconcile predestination with commands.

Key Terms
المعاني
سبعة
علمه
حياته
قدرة
إرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some consider the attributes of meaning to be merely names or relations without real existence.
Correction: The passage affirms they are real attributes that subsist in the essence ('the attributes of meaning are seven'), meaning they are not mere concepts.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how many attributes of meaning are there?
A) Four
B) Seven
C) Ten
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The seven attributes of meaning are real, distinct perfections in God's essence, known through revelation and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim God's knowledge encompasses all things, including your most secret thoughts. When you sinned today—even in your heart—did that belief stop you? If not, what does that reveal about the reality of your faith in this attribute? How will you act differently tomorrow when a temptation arises?
?
God is Living, Powerful, Willing—yet you struggle to surrender a single area of your life to His will. What is that area, and why do you cling to control? What would it mean for you to pray today, 'Your will, not mine,' and truly mean it?
?
The attribute of life in God is eternal and perfect. How does your fear of death or anxiety about the future expose a lack of trust in the Living God? What concrete step can you take this week to anchor your hope in His eternal life rather than in this temporary world?

The Distinction Between God's Will and His Command
Distinction between will and command

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ashʿarī distinction between God's will (irāda) and His command (amr), and why they can be opposite.

Core Idea
God may will something He does not command, and vice versa.

This lesson tackles a subtle theological point: the difference between what God wills (irāda) and what He commands (amr). The author clarifies that 'intention' (qaṣd) is distinct from 'command', resolving potential tensions between divine decrees and ethical commands.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the poem
Read the lines: 'And everything that is happening is what He willed. And if He may have commanded its opposite, then intention is different from command, so abandon dispute.'
2
Understand the statement
Everything that occurs is by God's will. But His command may be the opposite of what He wills (e.g., He commands good but wills trial).
This shows will and command are not identical.
3
Grasp the Ashʿarī position
God's command is His revealed law (sharʿ), while His will is His creative decree (qadāʾ). They can differ because God may decree hardship while commanding obedience.
This solves the problem of evil and divine commands.
4
Reflect on 'intention' (qaṣd)
The author uses 'qaṣd' (intention) to mean the same as will? Actually qaṣd is often synonymous with irāda. The point is that God's intention (what He wants to happen) is different from what He commands humans to do.
This is a key Ashʿarī point to reconcile predestination with obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْمَعَانِي سَبْعَةُ للرَّائِي * أي عِلْمُهُ الْمُحِيطُ بِالأَشْيَاءِ حَياتُهُ وقُدْرَةٌ إرادة * وكُلُّ شيءٍ كَائِنْ أَرَادَة وإنْ يَكُنْ بِضِدِّهِ قَدْ أَمَرا * فالقَصْدُ غيرُ الأمرِ فاطرَح المِرَا
Then the attributes of meaning are seven for the seer: that is, His knowledge encompassing all things, His life, power, will. And everything that is happening is what He willed. And if He may have commanded its opposite, then intention is different from command, so abandon dispute.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage lists the seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt ma'ānī). The author states they are seven: knowledge ('ilm), life (ḥayāh), power (qudra), will (irāda), and by implication hearing, sight, and speech (from later lines). He emphasizes that God's knowledge encompasses all things, and everything that occurs is by His will (irāda). He also makes a distinction: God's command (amr) may sometimes be opposite to His will (e.g., He commands good but wills trial). Thus, 'intention' (qaṣd) is not identical to 'command'—this is a key Ashʿarī point to reconcile predestination with commands.

Key Terms
إرادة
القصد
الأمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that whatever God commands, He must also will to happen, otherwise there is a contradiction.
Correction: The passage clarifies that God may command something while willing its opposite; these are different aspects of the divine will (legislative vs. creative).

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between God's will and His command according to this passage?
A) They are identical.
B) Command is a subset of will.
C) They can be different: He may will what He does not command.
D) Command overrides will.

Key Takeaway
God's will and command are distinct; He may will something that He does not command, and vice versa.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or see evil in the world, do you sometimes think that God would not will such things? How does the truth that everything happening is by His will change your perspective? Will you trust His wisdom even when you cannot understand why He wills what He commands against?
?
The author says 'abandon dispute' about this distinction. Is there a theological question you have been struggling with that requires humble acceptance rather than full resolution? Are you willing to submit to God’s revealed truth even if your mind cannot fully reconcile His will and command?
?
If all that happens is willed by God, including your own sins, does that make you complacent about sinning? Or does the distinction that God still commands obedience and holds you accountable motivate you to strive harder? How can you live with both trust in God’s will and earnest effort to obey His command?

Divine Attributes

The Eternal Attributes of Speech, Hearing, and Sight
Affirmation and explanation of three eternal attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attributes of speech, hearing, and sight are eternal and how they relate to their objects.

Core Idea
God's attributes are eternal because they are not separate from His essence.

This lesson unpacks a key passage from the matn that affirms three divine attributes—speech, hearing, and sight—and explains their eternal nature. The author also clarifies how these attributes attach to different categories of existence. Understanding this ground prepares you for the more specific discussion of divine speech in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice that the author begins by referring to 'four divisions' in existing things.
These four divisions are necessary, impossible, possible, and perhaps another—but the text doesn't list them here.
2
Identify the attributes mentioned
Focus on the second line: 'His speech, hearing, and sight'. These are the three attributes discussed in this section.
3
Understand the attachment rules
The passage specifies which attributes attach to which objects: knowledge and speech attach to all four divisions; power and will attach to all possibilities; hearing and sight attach to every existing thing that is seen.
This shows that God's attributes comprehensively relate to all aspects of reality.
4
Grasp the basis of eternity
The author states that all attributes are eternal 'in essence' because they are 'not other than the essence'. This means they are not created or acquired.
This is a foundational Ash'ari principle: attributes are real but not separate entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَقَد عَلِمتَ أربَعًا أَقْسَامَا * فِي الْكَائِنَاتِ فَاحْفَظِ الْمَقَامَا كَلامُهُ والسَّمْعُ والإِبْصَارُ * فَهُوَ الإِلهُ الفَاعِلُ الْمُخْتَارُ وَوَاجِبٌ تَعْلِيقُ ذِي الصِّفَاتِ * حَتْمًا دَوَامَـا مَـا عَـدَا الْحَيَاةِ فَالْعِلْمُ جَزْمًا وَالْكَلَامُ السَّامِي * تَعَلَّقَا بِسَائِرِ الْأَقْسَام وَقَدْرَةٌ إِرَادَةٌ تَعَلَّقَا * بِالْمُمْكِنَاتِ كُلْهَا أَخَا التَّقَى وَاجْزِمْ بِأَنَّ سَمْعَهُ وَالْبَصَرَا * تَعَلَّقَا بِكُلِّ مَوْجُودٍ يُرَى وَكُلُّهَا قَدِيْمَةٌ بِالذَّاتِ * لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِغَيْرِ الذَّاتِ ثُمَّ الْكَلَامُ لَيْسَ بِالْحُرُوفِ * وَلَيْسَ بِالتَّرْتِيبِ كَالْمَأْلُوفِ
So you have known four divisions in existing things, so preserve the station. His speech, hearing, and sight; and He is the God, the Agent, the Chooser. And it is necessary that the attachment of these attributes is necessarily perpetual except for life. Knowledge certainly and the sublime speech are attached to all divisions. Power and will are attached to all possible things, O pious brother. And be certain that His hearing and sight are attached to every existing thing that is seen. And all of them are eternal in essence because they are not other than the essence. Then speech is not in letters nor in arrangement as is customary.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage covers several points. First, it mentions four divisions in existing things (probably necessary, impossible, possible, and something else). Then it affirms that God's speech (kalām), hearing (sam'), and sight (baṣar) are attributes, and God is the 'Agent, the Chooser' (al-fā'il al-mukhtār). Next, it explains how these attributes relate to objects: knowledge and speech attach to all divisions, power and will attach to all possible things, and hearing and sight attach to every existing thing that is seen. A crucial point: all these attributes are eternal (qadīma) 'in essence' (bi-dhāt), 'because they are not other than the essence' (laysat bi-ghayr al-dhāt)—meaning they are not separate entities but real attributes. Finally, it specifies that God's speech is not composed of letters or sounds, nor does it have sequence, unlike human speech. This upholds the Ashʿarī doctrine of the eternal, uncreated speech of God (kalām nafsī).

Key Terms
كلامه
السمع
الإبصار
قديمة بالذات
ليست بغير الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'not other than the essence' means the attributes are identical to the essence (i.e., God is knowledge, etc., without distinction).
Correction: Ashʿarīs hold that attributes are eternal and inherent, but they are not the essence itself nor separate entities. They are real, non-identical properties.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which attributes attach to all four divisions?
A) Power and will
B) Knowledge and speech
C) Hearing and sight
D) Life and will

Key Takeaway
God's attributes of speech, hearing, and sight are eternal because they are not separate from His essence, and they relate to all aspects of reality according to their natures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if God's hearing and sight are attached to everything you do, including the moments no one else sees? What one habit would you need to change if you took this literally?
?
The passage declares that God's attributes are eternal and not separate from His essence. Have you ever doubted that divine attribute like His mercy or justice could be temporary? How can you cement your certainty that they are constant?
?
If you truly believed that God's knowledge and speech encompass all categories of existence, including the impossible, how would that reshape your trust in Him when life feels uncertain?

The Nature of Divine Speech: Transcending Letters and Sounds
Denial of letters and arrangement in divine speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine speech is not composed of letters or sounds and has no sequential order.

Core Idea
God's speech is an eternal, attribute—not a temporal sequence of words.

This lesson focuses on a crucial distinction in Ashʿarī theology: the uncreated speech of God (kalām nafsī) versus created human speech. The matn clarifies that divine speech is not made of letters or arranged in a sequence as human language is. This preserves God's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Focus on the last two lines of the passage. They directly state what divine speech is not.
The denial of letters and arrangement is absolute.
2
Contrast with human speech
Human speech consists of letters arranged in sequence. The author denies both for God.
This is a fundamental Ash'ari position against the Mu'tazila who said the Quran is created.
3
Connect to previous lesson
Recall that speech is eternal and attached to all divisions. Here we learn its nature: it is not a physical or temporal phenomenon.
4
Reflect on implications
If divine speech is without letters or order, it cannot be recited in parts or broken into verses. The recited Quran is an expression of that eternal speech.
This protects the belief that the Quran is uncreated as the word of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception: Some think that since the Quran is the word of God, it must be composed of letters and sounds like human speech.

B) Letters and arrangement

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you sense that you are uttering sounds that are a mere shadow of an eternal, unlettered reality, or do you feel you are producing the very speech of God? How would your reverence change if you deeply believed your tongue is only a vessel, and the true speech is beyond your lips? Pause right now and repeat one verse silently, focussing on its eternal meaning rather than the words.
?
If God's speech has no arrangement, then His command 'Be' is not a sequence of thought. Reflect: do you trust that God's single, eternal speech encompasses all His commands and decrees at once? How does this affect your patience in waiting for His promises? Write down one command of God you find hard to obey, and ask yourself if you have reduced it to a mere letter or sequence you can postpone.
?
You have read that divine speech is not 'as is customary'—meaning it does not resemble human speech. Are there ways you have been imagining God's speech as too human, perhaps as a voice that can be tired or interrupted? What would change in your dua if you spoke to a God whose speech is not limited by breath or time? Make a commitment to address God in your next prayer with the awareness that His eternal speech is hearing you right now.

The Impossibility of Opposites of God's Attributes
Proof that opposites of God's attributes are impossible and entail poverty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the opposites of God's perfect attributes are impossible, based on the argument that they would imply neediness in God.

Core Idea
Opposites of God's attributes are impossible because they would make Him needy.

This lesson examines a concise proof from the matn that the opposites of God's attributes are rationally impossible. The proof uses the concept of poverty (faqr) to show that any deficiency would contradict God's absolute self-sufficiency. Let's read the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic verse once and its literal translation. Pay attention to the flow from the condition to the conclusion.
The rhyme scheme is not essential for the argument.
2
Identify the logical structure
Notice the conditional argument: 'If He were not described with them, He would be known by other attributes.' Then it says such a being would be in ultimate poverty. But God is self-sufficient.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: assuming the opposite leads to an impossible consequence.
3
Connect to the conclusion
Since opposites of attributes would imply neediness, and God is absolutely free of need, those opposites are impossible.
This reinforces the necessity of affirming God's perfect attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَسْتَحِيلُ ضِدُّ مَا تَقَدَّمَا * مِنَ الصَّفاتِ الشَّامخات فاعلما لِأَنَّهُ لَوْلَمْ يَكُنْ مَوْصُوفا * بِهَا لَكَانَ بِالسِّوَى مَعْرُوفا وَكُلُّ مَنْ قَامَ بِهِ سِوَاهَا * فَهُوَ الذِي فِي الفَقْرِ قَدْ تَنَاهَى وَالوَاحِدُ الْمَعْبُودُ لا يَفْتَقِرُ * لِغَيْرِهِ جَلَّ الغَنِي الْمُقْتَدِرُ
And the opposite of what preceded from the lofty attributes is impossible, so know. Because if He were not described with them, He would be known by other than them. And everyone in whom other than them subsists, he is the one who has reached utmost poverty. And the One, the Worshipped, does not need others, Exalted is the Self-Sufficient, the Omnipotent.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage argues that the opposites of God's perfect attributes (e.g., ignorance, death, weakness) are impossible. The proof: if God were not described with these attributes, He would be known by other attributes (deficient ones), which is not fitting. Then, any being that has qualities other than these perfect attributes is in ultimate poverty (faqr)—meaning neediness. But God is free of need (ghani) and has no need of anything. Therefore, He must possess perfection. Thus, affirming God's attributes is necessary to avoid attributing need to Him.

Key Terms
ضد
الصفات الشامخات
الفقر
الغني
المقتدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God could have some perfect attributes and some deficient ones.
Correction: The argument shows that any deficiency implies poverty, which would contradict God's absolute self-sufficiency. Therefore, all of God's attributes must be perfect.

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence if God were not described with perfect attributes?
A) He would be unknown.
B) He would be described by other, deficient attributes.
C) He would become originated.
D) He would be dependent on creation.

Key Takeaway
Opposites of God's attributes are impossible because they would necessitate neediness, contradicting His self-sufficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel independent in your life, do you realize that every moment you are utterly dependent on the Self-Sufficient One? How will you acknowledge your poverty today?
?
If the opposite of any of God's attributes is impossible because it would make Him needy, then what does your doubt or neglect of His attributes say about your understanding of His perfection? Will you repent and affirm them?
?
You worship a God who cannot be described with any deficiency. Are there any beliefs in your heart that attribute imperfection to God? Expose them now and replace them with this truth.

Necessity and Eternity of Attribute Attachment
Stanza on the necessary and eternal attachment of divine attributes except life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the attachment of divine attributes is necessary and eternal, with the exception of the attribute of life.

Core Idea
The attachment of all attributes except life is eternally necessary.

This first stanza sets the foundational rule for all divine attributes: their attachment to God's essence is not temporary but everlasting. The exception of life hints at a deeper distinction among attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the stanza carefully
Read the Arabic line once and then the translation. Notice the words 'واجب' and 'دواما' which indicate necessity and eternity.
2
Identify the exception
The stanza says 'ما عدا الحياة' – except life. Ask yourself why life might be an exception. The commentary will explain.
3
Reflect on the implication
If attachment is necessary and eternal, then attributes are not accidental. This guards against the idea that God acquires attributes over time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَوَاجِبٌ تَعْلِيقُ ذِي الصِّفَاتِ * حَتْمًا دَوَامًا مَا عَدَا الْحَيَاةِ . فَالْعِلْمُ جَزْمًا وَالْكَلَامُ السَّامِي * تَعَلَّقَا بِسَائِرِ الْأَقْسَامِ . وَقُدْرَةٌ إِرَادَةٌ تَعَلَّقَا * بِالْمُمْكِنَاتِ كُلِّهَا أَخَا التُّقَى . وَاجْزِمْ بِأَنَّ سَمْعَهُ وَالْبَصَرًا * تَعَلَّقَا بِكُلِّ مَوْجُودٍ يُرَى . وَكُلُّهَا قَدِيمَةٌ بِالذَّاتِ * لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِغَيْرِ الذَّاتِ . ثُمَّ الْكَلَامُ لَيْسَ بِالْحُرُوفِ * وَلَيْسَ بِالتَّرْتِيبِ كَالْمَأْلُوفِ
And it is necessary that the attachment of the One with attributes * is permanently eternal except for life. So knowledge definitely, and the lofty speech * they are attached to the rest of the categories. And power and will are attached * to all possibles, O brother of piety. And be certain that His hearing and sight * are attached to every existent that is seen. And all of them are eternal by the essence * because they are not other than the essence. Then speech is not with letters * and not with arrangement as is customary.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents a series of stanzas on the divine attributes. It first states that the attachment of attributes to God is necessary and eternal, except for the attribute of life (which may have a special rule). Then it specifies that knowledge and speech are attached to all categories of things. Power and will are attached to all possible things. Hearing and sight are attached to every existent that can be perceived. The passage then asserts that all these attributes are eternal by essence, meaning they are not separate from God's essence. Finally, it clarifies that divine speech is not composed of letters or arranged in a sequential manner like human speech.

Key Terms
تعلق
واجب
دوام
حياة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's attributes are temporary or that He acquires them after being without them.
Correction: This verse affirms that attachment is necessary and eternal, meaning God has always been knowing, powerful, etc., except life which is His essence.

Checkpoint
According to this stanza, which attribute is excepted from the rule of eternal attachment?
A) Knowledge
B) Life
C) Power
D) Speech

Key Takeaway
All divine attributes except life have an attachment that is both necessary and eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If all of God's attributes (except life) are eternally attached to Him, can His mercy, justice, or power ever be withdrawn from you? How does this certainty affect your trust in Him today?
?
The lesson says life is the exception—it is intrinsic, not an external attachment. Do you truly believe that your own life and the life of everything comes from God's very essence? How would you live differently if you internalized this?
?
When you face trials, do you ever doubt that God's attributes are still permanently attached to Him—that His mercy and wisdom are still fully present? What concrete step can you take today to strengthen your conviction in the unchanging nature of His attributes?

Universal Attachment of Knowledge and Speech
Stanza on the universal attachment of knowledge and speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine knowledge and speech attach to all categories of things.

Core Idea
God's knowledge and speech encompass every category of existence.

After establishing the general rule, the poem specifies that two attributes—knowledge and speech—have universal scope. They are not limited to certain types of objects.

Guided Path
1
Read the stanza
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the word 'جزما' (definitely) which emphasizes certainty.
2
Understand 'all categories'
What are the categories? The commentary explains that knowledge and speech cover all existents, past, present, future, and even impossibilities as objects of knowledge.
3
Contrast with other attributes
Compare with the next stanzas: power and will have a different scope (only possibles), hearing and sight have a different scope (only perceived existents).

Source Text

?

?
God's speech is not limited to the Quran or any revealed book—it encompasses all categories, even things that do not exist. ?

Attachment of Power and Will to Possibles
Stanza on the attachment of power and will to all possible things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine power and will are attached only to possible things.

Core Idea
God's power and will extend to every possible thing.

This stanza narrows the scope: unlike knowledge and speech, power and will are limited to the realm of possibilities. This is a crucial distinction in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the stanza
Read and translate. Notice the phrase 'أخا التقى' is a rhetorical address.
2
Understand 'possibles'
Possibles are things that can exist or not exist. God's power and will apply to all of them, but not to necessary or impossible things.
3
Compare with knowledge
Knowledge includes even impossible things (e.g., a partner to God is known to be impossible), but power does not extend to impossibilities.

Stanza on the attachment of hearing and sight to perceived existents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's hearing and sight attach to every existent that is perceivable.

Core Idea
God hears all sounds and sees all visible things.

This stanza addresses the attributes of hearing and sight, limiting their attachment to existent things that are heard or seen. This prevents anthropomorphism while affirming that God perceives everything.

Guided Path
1
Read the stanza
Read and translate. Note the imperative 'اجزم' – be certain.
2
Understand the scope
The scope is 'every existent that is seen' meaning every existing thing that can be perceived. This includes all material existents, but not abstract concepts.
3
Contrast with other attributes
Unlike knowledge which covers all categories, hearing and sight are limited to perceptible existents.

Eternity of Attributes by Essence
Stanza asserting the eternity of attributes by identity with essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all divine attributes are eternal by virtue of being identical with God's essence.

Core Idea
The attributes are eternal because they are not separate from God's essence.

This critical stanza explains the basis for the eternity of attributes: they are not entities distinct from God's essence. This safeguards divine unity and avoids multiplicity in God.

Guided Path
1
Read the stanza
Read and translate. Note 'قديمة بالذات' – eternal by essence.
2
Understand the reasoning
The reason given: 'because they are not other than the essence'. This means the attributes are not accidental additions; they are the very essence in its aspects.
3
Reflect on the implications
If attributes were separate, they would be created (muhdath). By being identical with essence, they are eternal. This is a cornerstone of Sunni theology.

Nature of Divine Speech: Beyond Letters
Stanza negating letter and arrangement in divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine speech is not composed of letters or sequential arrangement like human speech.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal and non-composite, unlike human language.

This concluding stanza clarifies the nature of the attribute of speech, rejecting any notion that God's speech is material or sequential. This distinguishes the eternal attribute from the revealed scriptures.

Guided Path
1
Read the stanza
Read and translate. Note 'ليس بالحروف' – not with letters.
2
Understand what it negates
It negates two characteristics: letters (huruf) and arrangement (tartib). These are accidental properties of created speech.
3
Reflect on the implication
If speech is not letters or arrangement, then it is an eternal attribute without composition. This means the Qur'an as revealed is an expression of this attribute, but the attribute itself is not created.

Impossibility of Opposites of Divine Attributes
Proof that opposites of divine attributes entail neediness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the opposites of Allah's perfect attributes are impossible, based on the rational proof that lacking them would imply neediness.

Core Idea
Opposites of divine attributes are impossible because they would imply neediness in Allah.

This lesson examines a key argument from the matn: why Allah cannot possess the opposites of His perfect attributes. The author presents a concise proof: if Allah were not described with these attributes, He would be described with their opposites, which would entail neediness. Since Allah is absolutely independent, such opposites are impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic couplet and its translation. Notice the structure: the claim is stated first, then the reason, then the conclusion.
The poetic form compresses the argument; pay attention to each line.
2
Understand the logical reasoning
Break down the conditional argument: If Allah were not described with the perfect attributes, He would be described with their opposites. Having opposites subsisting in Him would mean He is in need (poverty).
The proof uses a reductio ad absurdum: assuming the opposite leads to an impossibility.
3
Apply to divine perfection
Reflect on why this proof establishes the necessity of attributes. Since Allah is absolutely independent (al-Ghani), He must possess these perfect attributes to avoid neediness.
This connects to the broader theme of Allah's self-sufficiency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَسْتَحِيلُ ضِدُّ مَا تَقَدَّمَا * مِنَ الصِّفَاتِ الشَّامِخَاتِ فَاعْلَمَا . لِأَنَّهُ لَوْلَمْ يَكُنْ مَوْصُوفًا * بِهَا لَكَانَ بِالسِّوَى مَعْرُوفًا . وَكُلُّ مَنْ قَامَ بِهِ سِوَاهَا * فَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي الْفَقْرِ قَدْ تَنَاهَى
And the opposite of what has preceded from the lofty attributes is impossible, so know. Because if He were not described with them, He would be known by something else. And whoever has something other than them (i.e., the attributes) subsisting in him, then he is the one who has reached the utmost poverty.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the necessity of divine attributes. It states that the opposites of the attributes mentioned earlier (such as ignorance, weakness, etc.) are impossible for God. The reason is that if God were not described with these perfect attributes, He would be described with their opposites. And anything that has an opposite attribute subsisting in it is in need of that attribute and therefore in a state of poverty. Since God is absolutely independent, He must possess these perfect attributes.

Key Terms
استحالة
ضد
صفت
فقر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The opposites of divine attributes are merely unlikely, not logically impossible.
Correction: According to this proof, they are logically impossible because they would entail neediness, which contradicts Allah's absolute independence.

Checkpoint
Why is the opposite of the divine attributes impossible?
A) Because God is powerful
B) Because He would then be known by something else and thus be in need
C) Because the attributes are unnecessary
D) Because the opposite is not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Opposites of divine attributes are impossible because they would entail neediness, contradicting Allah's absolute independence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is free from all opposites of His perfect attributes, what does that mean for your own neediness? Are you acknowledging your poverty before Him every day, or do you live as if you are independent?
?
The proof shows that for Allah, having opposite attributes is impossible because it implies need. How often do you attribute to Allah human-like flaws in your heart, even if you deny them with your tongue? What would it take to truly internalize His absolute perfection?
?
When you face your own weaknesses and failures, do you run to the One who has no weakness, or do you try to fill your poverty with created things? What one concrete habit will you change today to turn from your own 'filling' to His sufficiency?

God's Independence and Freedom from Obligation
Three stanzas affirming God's independence and denying necessity in His acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God is completely independent and not subject to any obligation, including the obligation to do what is beneficial for creation.

Core Idea
God owes nothing to anyone.

This passage from al-Kharida strikes at the heart of how we should think about God's actions. It affirms that God is self-sufficient and not bound by any external necessity. The author uses a direct, powerful style to reject any notion of duty imposed on the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic stanza and its English translation. Notice the rhythm and rhyme of the original.
2
Identify the key claims
Identify three things: God's independence, His free choice in actions, and the condemnation of imposing obligations.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Think about why this matters: if God were obliged to act in certain ways, He would not be fully independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْوَاحِدُ الْمَعْبُودُ لَا يَفْتَقِرُ * لِغَيْرِهِ جَلَّ الْغَنِيُّ الْمُقْتَدِرُ . وَجَائِزٌ فِي حَقِّهِ الْإِيجَادُ * وَالتَّرْكُ وَالْإِشْقَاءُ وَالْإِسْعَادُ . وَمَنْ يَقُلْ فِعْلُ الصَّلَاحِ وَجَبَا * عَلَى الْإِلَهِ قَدْ أَسَاءَ الْأَدَبَا
And the One worshipped does not need anyone else, exalted is the Independent, the Powerful. And it is possible in His right to create, and to leave, and to make miserable, and to make happy. And whoever says that doing what is beneficial is obligatory upon God has indeed misbehaved.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage emphasizes God's absolute independence and freedom. It states that the One worshipped does not need anything other than Himself. It then lists possible actions for God: to create or not to create, to cause misery or happiness. All these are within His power and not obligatory. Finally, it condemns the view that God is obliged to do what is beneficial for creatures, calling such a claim a breach of proper etiquette towards God.

Key Terms
الْغَنِيُّ
الْمُقْتَدِرُ
جَائِزٌ
الْإِيجَادُ
التَّرْكُ
الْإِشْقَاءُ
الْإِسْعَادُ
الصَّلَاحِ
وَجَبَا
أَدَبَا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God is obliged to act in the best interest of His creatures, e.g., to always do what is beneficial.
Correction: The passage states that God is free and not under any obligation, even to do good. His actions are by His will, not by any external necessity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on saying that doing good is obligatory upon God?
A) It is a correct statement
B) It is a sign of respect
C) It is misbehaviour
D) It is a duty

Key Takeaway
God is absolutely independent and free; He is not obligated to do any action, even what is beneficial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When life is hard, do you ever feel that God owes you an easier path? How does this passage challenge that feeling, and what would it look like for you to let go of that entitlement today?
?
If God is not obligated to do anything for you, does your gratitude become more sincere or more strained? Will you thank Him for every small mercy, knowing He could have withheld it?
?
The passage calls it misbehavior to say God must do good. Are there any places in your heart where you demand God to act a certain way? How can you repent from that and instead submit to His absolute freedom?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
Affirming the Beatific Vision of God
A stanza affirming the beatific vision with rational and textual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the vision of God in Paradise is a certain doctrine supported by both rational possibility and textual proof.

Core Idea
Seeing God in Paradise is rationally possible and textually proven.

This lesson presents a foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunna: the beatific vision (ru'yat Allah) in the afterlife. The poet commands certainty in this doctrine and provides its twin supports – reason ('aql) and revelation (naql). Let's examine the stanza and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic stanza
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the rhyming and the command 'wajzim' (be certain).
The stanza is concise but packs a complete argument.
2
Identify the two parts
The stanza has a command (first hemistich) and a justification (second hemistich). The justification itself has two components: rational possibility and textual evidence.
3
Understand 'jā'iz bil-'aql'
In kalam, 'jā'iz' means logically possible—not necessary and not impossible. The vision is possible because God is existent and can make Himself seen if He wills.
4
Appreciate the role of naql
Textual evidence (Quran and Sunnah) confirms what reason deems possible. This reinforces certainty (jizm).
5
Reflect on certainty
The command 'wajzim' indicates that this is not optional belief but a required conviction. Consider why certainty is demanded.
Certainty here means firm belief without doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاجْزِمْ أَخِي بِرُؤْيَةِ الْإِلَهِ * فِي جَنَّةِ الْخُلْدِ بِلَا تَنَاهِي . إِذِ الْوُقُوعُ جَائِزٌ بِالْعَقْلِ * وَقَدْ أَتَى فِيهِ دَلِيلُ النَّقْلِ
And be certain, my brother, of seeing God in the eternal paradise without end. For the occurrence is possible by reason, and the textual evidence has come for it.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This short stanza affirms the doctrine of the beatific vision (ru'yat Allah) in the afterlife. It commands the reader to be certain (jizm) that the believers will see God in Paradise eternally. It gives two justifications: first, it is rationally possible, because God is existent and visible if He wills; second, there is transmitted evidence (naql) from the Quran and Sunnah proving it.

دليل النقل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Seeing God is a physical, bodily vision like seeing a material object.
Correction: The vision is not physical or anthropomorphic; it is a direct, unveiled vision of God without modality, suitable to His majesty.

Checkpoint

C) Both reason and revelation

Key Takeaway
The beatific vision is a certain doctrine supported by both reason and revelation.

The Prophet's Superiority Through Divine Selection
Commentary on the Prophet's superiority with a hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet Muhammad's superiority over all creation is established through Allah's deliberate choice of his lineage, as shown in an authentic hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet is the best of the best because Allah chose him from the best lineages.

This lesson opens the poem with praise and then dives into the commentary's central claim: the Prophet's unmatched status over all beings, even other prophets, is rooted in divine selection. The commentary invokes a powerful hadith that traces a chain of chosen lineages leading directly to the Prophet. Pay close attention to the hadith's structure—it is the proof for this doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic opening and translation
Start by reading the Arabic verses of praise and then the commentary sentence. Notice the tone of exaltation and the immediate focus on the Prophet's merit.
The opening verses praise Allah, then send blessings on the Prophet.
2
Identify the hadith in the passage
Find the hadith text within the commentary. It begins with 'إنَّ الله اصطفى...' and lists four levels of selection.
The hadith is authentic and serves as the core evidence.
3
Trace the chain of divine selection
List the four levels: from Ishmael's descendants, Allah chose Kinana; from Kinana, Quraysh; from Quraysh, Banu Hashim; and from Banu Hashim, the Prophet himself.
Each step narrows down to the best.
4
Understand the conclusion 'I am the best of the best of the best'
The Prophet's statement 'فأنا خيار من خيار من خيار' means he is the best from the best from the best. This establishes his superiority over all creation.
The triple 'خيار' emphasizes the highest level of excellence.

The Three Rational Categories: Wajib, Muhal, and Ja'iz
Definitions of wajib, muhal, and ja'iz for Allah and prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of the three rational categories (wajib, muhal, ja'iz) and how they apply to Allah and by extension to the prophets.

Core Idea
All rational judgments about Allah fall into three clear categories: necessary, impossible, and possible.

Before delving into detailed theological proofs, the commentator establishes the foundational vocabulary for discussing what is rationally necessary, impossible, or possible in relation to Allah. These three categories, known as al-wajib, al-muhal, and al-ja'iz, are the bedrock of kalam reasoning. This lesson presents their definitions and notes their application to the prophets as well.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three definitions
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting how each term is defined. Pay attention to the key phrase for each: 'لا يقبل الانتفاء' for wajib, 'لا يقبل الثبوت' for muhal, and 'يقبل الثبوت والانتفاء' for ja'iz.
2
Understand the extension to prophets
The commentator states that these same categories apply in respect to the messengers of Allah. Consider what that implies: the prophets also have necessary, impossible, and possible attributes in their capacity as messengers.
3
Review the grammatical and poetic notes
The passage includes notes on pronunciation and poetic meter. While secondary, they show the careful transmission of this knowledge. You may skip these if focusing on doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي: يَعرِفُ الواجِبَ والْمُحَالا * مَعْ جَائِز فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى ومِثْلُ ذَا فِي حَقِّ رُسُلِ اللَّهِ * عَليهِم تَحِيَّةُ الإِلَهِ - شرح الشيخ حسن محمد المشاط المكي المالكي (الواجب) في حقه تعالى وهو الثابت له تعالى الذي لا يقبل الانتفاء (۱). (والمحالا) أي: المستحيل في حقه تعالى، وهو ما لا يقبل الثبوت والألف فيه للإطلاق (۲). (مع) معرفة (جائز في حقه تعالى) وهو ما يقبل الثبوت والانتفاء. ومثل ذا أي معرفة مثل ذا أي المذكور من الواجب وما عطف عليه، في حق رُسل الله) بإسكان السين عند تميم عملًا بقاعدة قوله: وكُلُّ فُعْل بسكون العين * كاليسر والعُشر ونحو أُذن فَضَمُّ عَيْنِهِ يُرَى اتْبَاهَا * لِفَائِهِ عَنْ أَسَد قَد شَاءَا وفعل كعُنُقِ وطنبِ تَسْكِينُهُ إِلى تَمِيم انسبِ عليهم) بتحريك الميم بالضم أو الكسر للوزن (تحيَّةُ الإله) تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى. ثم شرع الناظم رحمه الله تعالى في تعريف الواجب العقلي، (۱) الانتفاء هو العدم والزوال، فالواجب حينئذ هو الأمر الثابت الذي لا يقبل الزوال. Meaning: He knows the wajib and the muhal * along with the ja'iz in respect to Him, Most High; and similar to this in respect to the messengers of Allah * upon them be the greeting of Allah. Commentary of Sheikh Hasan Muhammad al-Mashshāt al-Makki al-Maliki: (Al-wajib) in respect to Him, Most High, is that which is established for Him, Most High, which does not accept non-existence (1). (Al-muhalā) i.e., al-mustahīl in respect to Him, Most High, is that which does not accept existence, and the alif is for release (2). (With) knowledge of (al-ja'iz in respect to Him, Most High) is that which accepts existence and non-existence. And 'similar to this' means knowledge of the like of what was mentioned of al-wajib and what is coordinated with it, in respect to the messengers of Allah – with the sīn made sukun according to the Tamīm practice, following the rule of his statement: 'And every fa'l with sukun of the 'ayn... etc.' – 'upon them' with the mīm voweled with damm or kasr for meter 'the greeting of Allah' blessed and exalted. Then the versifier (al-nāzim) – may Allah have mercy on him – commenced the definition of the intellectual wajib. (1) Al-intifā' is non-existence and removal; so al-wajib then is the established matter that does not accept removal. (2) i.e., the release of the voice in the rhyme.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a poem that introduces the three rational categories (wajib, muhal, ja'iz) as they apply to Allah and the messengers. The commentator first defines each term in relation to Allah: al-wajib is that which is necessarily established for Allah and cannot be negated; al-muhal (or al-mustahīl) is that which cannot be established for Allah; al-ja'iz is that which could either be established or negated. He then notes that the same categories apply to the prophets in what is befitting them. The passage includes grammatical remarks about the pronunciation of 'rusul' and 'alayhim' for poetic meter. A footnote clarifies that 'al-intifā'' means non-existence or removal, reinforcing the definition of al-wajib. The passage ends with a transition to the definition of the intellectual wajib, which will be explained next.

Key Takeaway
The three rational categories—wajib, muhal, and ja'iz—define the boundaries of what can be said about Allah and the prophets, forming the basis for all theological arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah’s existence is wajib—absolutely necessary and impossible to negate. Does your heart truly accept that He cannot not exist? When you sin or neglect His commands, are you not acting as if His existence were optional? How would your life change if you woke each morning with the certainty that the Necessary Being is watching, and that you cannot escape His presence?
?
Prophets, too, have categories of wajib, muhal, and ja'iz. Is there any attribute you wrongly assume about a prophet—like thinking they could err in conveying revelation? How does knowing that it is muhal (impossible) for a prophet to lie about Allah affect your trust in the Quran and Sunnah? Will you let this certainty deepen your commitment to following their example?
?
Ja'iz means that Allah’s actions are not forced—He could will something or not. When you make dua, do you expect a certain outcome as if it were wajib? Does realizing that everything is possible for Allah humble you, or do you still feel entitled to your wishes? Will you surrender to His ja'iz will and trust that whatever He chooses is best?

Existence: A Necessary Divine Attribute
Commentator defines necessary existence and warns against relying on implication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why existence is a necessary attribute of Allah and how scholars distinguish between implied and explicitly established attributes.

Core Idea
Existence is the foundation; every divine perfection follows from it.

In this passage, Shaykh Hasan al-Mashat explains that the attribute of existence (wujud) is one of the necessary attributes of Allah. He emphasizes that while existence implies other perfections like pre-eternity, each attribute must be explicitly established by evidence rather than merely inferred. This lesson unpacks the definition of necessary existence and the methodological principle of not relying solely on implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own flow come through before interpreting.
Notice that the passage begins with a matn line followed by commentary.
2
Understand the definition of necessary existence
The passage defines necessary existence as that which does not admit of non-existence eternally. Reflect on what it means for something to be impossible to not exist.
3
Grasp the methodological point
The passage notes that scholars do not rely on implied indication alone; each attribute must be explicitly proven. Consider why this principle is important for systematic theology.
This connects to the broader method of Ilm al-Kalam.

صفة الوجود (ف) إذا علمت ما يجب على كلِّ مكلف من معرفة الواجب لله، والمستحيل عليه، والجائز له وعلمت الطريق الموصل إلى المعرفة ف (اعلم بأن (الوصف) أي اتصاف الله تعالى (بـ) صفة (الوجود من) أي: بعض (واجبات) الله (الواحد المعبود) تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى، فإن الواجبات لله تعالى كثيرة لا تنحصر ، لأن صفاته الكمالية لا تتناهى، قال الناظم في «شرحه» (۱) عقب ما ذكر: «إلا أنه لا يجب علينا تفصيل ما لم يقم عليه الدليل بالخصوص، بل الواجب أن نعتقد أن كمالاته تعالى لا تتناهى على الإجمال. وأما ما قام عليه الدليل بخصوصه فيجب اعتقاده تفصيلا، ثلاثة عشر صفة وأضدادها».

(۱) (ص ۱۷۷).
Section on Divine Matters
20 | So know that the description with existence * is among the necessary attributes of the One Worshiped.
Commentary by Sheikh Hasan al-Mashat al-Makki al-Maliki:
The attribute of existence: (So) if you know what is obligatory upon every legally accountable person regarding knowledge of what is necessary for Allah, what is impossible for Him, and what is possible for Him, and you know the path leading to knowledge, then know that the description (i.e., the attribute) of Allah Almighty with the attribute of existence is among the necessary attributes of Allah, the One Worshiped, Blessed and Exalted. Indeed, the necessary attributes of Allah are many and cannot be enumerated, because His perfect attributes are infinite. The author said in his commentary after what was mentioned: 'However, it is not obligatory upon us to detail what has not been specifically established by evidence; rather, it is obligatory to believe that His perfections are infinite in general. As for what has been specifically established by evidence, it is obligatory to believe it in detail: thirteen attributes and their opposites.' 
And they are?
The meaning of His existence being necessary: that it does not admit of negation eternally and everlastingly, i.e., its non-existence is impossible.
Benefit:
Establishing existence for Allah Almighty, even if it entails establishing pre-eternity (qidam) and everlastingness (baqa') for Him, does not suffice and does not relieve from mentioning them later, because the scholars of this art are not content with implied indication (dalalat al-iltizam).
(1) (p. 177).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining that the attribute of existence (wujud) is one of the necessary (wajib) attributes of Allah. It begins by quoting the poem: 'So know that the description with existence is among the necessary attributes of the One Worshiped.' The commentator then explains that after learning the three rational judgments (necessary, impossible, possible) and the path to knowledge, one must know that being described with existence is one of Allah's necessary attributes. The necessary attributes are many because Allah's perfections are infinite. However, we are only obligated to believe in detail those attributes for which specific evidence exists, namely thirteen attributes and their opposites. The passage then defines 'necessary existence': it does not admit of non-existence at any time, i.e., non-existence is impossible. Finally, a benefit is mentioned: establishing existence necessarily implies pre-eternity (qidam) and everlastingness (baqa'), but scholars do not rely on implication alone; they require explicit mention of each attribute. This is why the author will separately discuss qidam and baqa' later.

Key Terms
وجود
واجب
قدم
بقاء
دلالة الالتزام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Proving that existence is necessary for Allah is sufficient to prove all other attributes by implication.
Correction: Scholars of kalam require each attribute to be established by explicit evidence, not just implied from existence. Implication alone does not suffice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are scholars not content with merely implying pre-eternity and everlastingness from the proof of existence?
A) Because they consider these attributes unimportant
B) Because they require explicit mention for each attribute
C) Because existence does not imply other attributes
D) Because the author forgot to include them

Key Takeaway
Existence is a necessary attribute of Allah, meaning His non-existence is impossible, and scholars insist on explicit evidence for each attribute rather than relying on implication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly feel in your heart that your own existence is contingent and that Allah's existence is absolutely necessary, or do you live as if you are self-sufficient?
?
Are there attributes of Allah that you believe in only implicitly (e.g., 'He must have them because He exists') without stopping to affirm and contemplate each one explicitly—recognizing that your faith may be incomplete?
?
When you reflect on the fact that Allah's perfections are infinite and beyond enumeration, does that fill you with awe and motivate you to seek knowledge of His names and attributes, or do you remain content with a general belief?

The Necessity of God's Existence
Commentator explains that existence is a necessary attribute and defines its meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's existence is considered necessary in Islamic theology and what that means for His eternity.

Core Idea
God's existence is necessary—it cannot be negated, past or future.

Before delving into the detailed attributes of God, the commentator establishes that existence itself is a necessary attribute. This lesson explains the meaning of 'necessary existence' and why it is the foundation for other attributes. It also clarifies a common point: proving existence alone does not automatically prove pre-eternity without explicit evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how the commentator defines the attribute of existence as necessary.
The passage refers to prior knowledge of the three categories (necessary, impossible, possible).
2
Understand the definition
Focus on the line: 'the meaning of His existence being necessary is that it does not admit of non-existence eternally and forever.' This means God's existence has no beginning and no end.
3
Grasp the benefit about implication
The passage adds a benefit: proving existence implies pre-eternity, but scholars do not rely on implication alone. They require explicit belief in pre-eternity and everlastingness as separate attributes.
This counters the misconception that proving existence is enough.

فاعْلَمْ بأَنَّ الوَصْفَ بالوُجُودِ مِنْ وَاجِبَاتِ الوَاحِدِ الْمَعْبُودِ شرح الشيخ حسن محمد المشاط المكي المالكي ع صفة الوجود (ف) إذا علمت ما يجب على كلِّ مكلف من معرفة الواجب لله، والمستحيل عليه، والجائز له وعلمت الطريق الموصل إلى المعرفة ف (اعلم بأن (الوصف) أي اتصاف الله تعالى (بـ) صفة (الوجود من) أي: بعض (واجبات) الله (الواحد المعبود) تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى، فإن الواجبات لله تعالى كثيرة لا تنحصر ، لأن صفاته الكمالية لا تتناهى، قال الناظم في «شرحه» عقب ما ذكر: «إلا أنه لا يجب علينا تفصيل ما لم يقم عليه الدليل بالخصوص، بل الواجب أن نعتقد أن كمالاته تعالى لا تتناهى على الإجمال. وأما ما قام عليه الدليل بخصوصه فيجب اعتقاده تفصيلا، ثلاثة عشر صفة وأضدادها». وهي. و معنى كون وجوده واجبا: أنه لا يقبل الانتفاء أزلا وأبدًا، أي: لا يمكن عدمه. فائدة: إثبات الوجود الله تعالى وإن كان يستلزم ثبوت القدم والبقاء له، فإن ذلك لا يكفي ولا يغني عن ذكرهما فيما يأتي، لأن علماء هذا الفن لا يكتفون بدلالة الالتزام.
Know that the attribute of existence is among the obligatory (attributes) of the One who is worshipped. Commentary by Sheikh Hasan Muhammad al-Mashat al-Makki al-Maliki: The attribute of existence. (F) If you have known what is obligatory upon every legally responsible person from knowledge of what is necessary for God, what is impossible for Him, and what is possible for Him, and you have known the path leading to knowledge, then (know that the attribute, i.e., God's being described with the attribute of existence, is from among, i.e., some of, the necessary attributes of God, the One who is worshipped, Blessed and Exalted. For the necessary attributes of God are many and cannot be counted because His attributes of perfection are infinite. The author said in his commentary following what was mentioned: 'Except that it is not obligatory upon us to detail what has not been specifically established by evidence; rather, it is obligatory to believe in general that His perfections are infinite. As for what has been specifically established by evidence, it is obligatory to believe in detail: thirteen attributes and their opposites.' And they are. And the meaning of His existence being necessary is that it does not admit of non-existence eternally and forever, i.e., its non-existence is impossible. Benefit: Proving existence for God Almighty, even if it entails establishing pre-eternity and everlastingness for Him, that is not sufficient and does not dispense with mentioning them later, because the scholars of this art are not satisfied with implied indication (dalalat al-iltizam).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation. It begins by stating the poetic line that the attribute of existence is among the necessary attributes of God. The commentator then explains the context: one must first know the three categories (necessary, impossible, possible) for God and the path to knowledge. Then he elaborates that the attribute of existence is one of God's necessary attributes, but there are many such attributes because God's perfections are infinite. He quotes the author to note that we are only required to believe in detail those attributes for which specific evidence exists (thirteen attributes and their opposites); others we believe in generally. Then he defines the meaning of existence being necessary: it cannot be non-existent eternally, past and future. Finally, he adds a useful note: proving existence implies pre-eternity and everlastingness, but scholars of kalam do not rely on implication (dalalat al-iltizam) alone; they require explicit mention.

Key Terms
الوصف بالوجود
واجبات الله
صفات الكمال
ثلاثة عشر صفة
القدم والبقاء
دلالة الالتزام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Proving that God exists is enough to also prove that He is eternal.
Correction: While existence implies pre-eternity and everlastingness, the scholars of kalam do not rely on implication; they require explicit evidence and belief in each attribute separately.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of God's existence being 'wajib'?
A) It is possible but not necessary.
B) It cannot be negated eternally.
C) It is only in the mind.
D) It is contingent on creation.

Key Takeaway
God's existence is necessary and does not admit non-existence; though it logically implies pre-eternity, explicit belief in each attribute is required.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that God's existence is necessary and does not admit non-existence—past, present, or future. Does your daily life reflect this certainty, or do you sometimes live as if His existence were optional? What specific habit would change if you truly internalized that He cannot not exist?
?
The scholars warn that implied indication (dalalat al-iltizam) is not sufficient; explicit belief is required. Are there aspects of your faith where you rely on vague assumptions rather than seeking clear, evidence-based conviction? Will you commit to studying one attribute of God explicitly this week?
?
God's perfections are infinite and cannot be fully detailed without evidence. How does this humbling truth affect your worship? Do you ever feel satisfied with minimal knowledge, or do you actively seek to know more of His names and attributes? What is one step you will take to deepen your knowledge of a specific attribute?
