The Nafsiyyah Attribute: Existence Identical to Essence
Commentator defines the nafsiyyah attribute and distinguishes it from other attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the nafsiyyah (essential) attribute and how it differs from other divine attributes.

Core Idea
The nafsiyyah attribute is existence itself, not an added quality.

In this passage, the commentator explains the first type of divine attribute: the nafsiyyah attribute, also called essential. He defines it as the attribute without which the essence cannot be conceived, and clarifies that it is identical to the essence itself, unlike other attributes that indicate additional meanings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage from the matn and the commentary. Then read the literal English translation to grasp the flow.
The passage begins with the matn line and then the commentary.
2
Identify the definition and key characteristics
Look for the definition: 'the attribute without which the essence is not conceivable.' Note that it is an affirmative attribute that indicates the essence itself, not an added meaning.
This attribute is called nafsiyyah because it relates to the essence (nafs).
3
Distinguish from other attributes
Observe how the commentator excludes attributes of meanings like power: those indicate an additional meaning beyond the essence. The nafsiyyah attribute is unique in being identical to the essence.
This distinction is crucial in Ash'ari theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذِي تُسَمَّى صِفةٌ نَفْسِيَّةٌ * ثُمَّ تَلِيهَا خَمْسَةٌ سَلْبِيَّة

شرح الشيخ حسن محمد المشاط المكي المالكي:
الصفة النفسية (وذي) أي وهذه الصفة، وهي صفة الوجود، (تسمى: صفة نفسية منسوبة إلى النفس أي الذات، ومعناها: الصفة التي لا تُعقَلُ الذات بدونها.
وتُعرَّف بأنها: صفة ثبوتية، يدل الوصف بها على نفس الذات أي: لا على معنى زائد على الذات.
وخرج صفات المعاني نحو القدرة، والمغوية، فإن الوصف بهما يدل على معنى زائد على الذات، ولا يدل الوصف على نفس الذات.
And this is called an attribute of essence (nafsiyyah). Then follow five negative attributes. Commentary by Sheikh Hasan Muhammad al-Mashat al-Maliki: The attribute of essence (nafsiyyah) – (Widhi) meaning: this attribute, which is the attribute of existence, is called an attribute of essence, attributed to the essence, i.e., the self. Its meaning: the attribute without which the essence is not conceivable. And it is defined as: an affirmative attribute, whose description indicates the essence itself, i.e., not an additional meaning to the essence. And it excludes the attributes of meanings, such as power and the derived (ma'nawiyyah), for describing by them indicates an additional meaning to the essence, and does not indicate the essence itself.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of the first type of divine attribute: the nafsiyyah (essential) attribute. The commentator begins by quoting the matn line that introduces this attribute, then explains it. The nafsiyyah attribute is the attribute of existence (wujud). It is called 'nafsiyyah' because it relates to the essence itself. The definition: it is an attribute without which the essence is not conceivable. It is an affirmative (thubutiyyah) attribute that indicates the essence itself, not an additional meaning. This distinguishes it from other affirmative attributes like power, which indicate a meaning superadded to the essence.

Key Terms
صفة نفسية
صفة ثبوتية
صفات المعاني
الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the attribute of existence is an additional attribute like power, separate from the essence.
Correction: The nafsiyyah attribute (existence) is identical to the essence itself, not a superadded quality.

Checkpoint
What is the nafsiyyah attribute?
A) Power
B) Existence
C) Knowledge
D) Will

Key Takeaway
The nafsiyyah attribute is existence itself, identical to the divine essence, and is defined as the attribute without which the essence cannot be conceived.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's existence is not just a property He has, but is His very essence, then He cannot not exist. Does this truth make you feel more secure in His promises? Take a moment to thank Him for being Al-Qayyum, the Self-Subsisting, and commit to relying only on Him today.
?
Your own existence is contingent—it is an added quality given by God. How often do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What is one habit you can change tonight to remind yourself that your existence is a gift, not a given?
?
The nafsiyyah attribute shows that God's essence is simple and not composed of parts. Do you ever think of God as having 'parts' or attributes that could be added or removed? How can you guard your heart against such subtle anthropomorphism? Write one ayat or hadith that affirms His oneness and keep it visible today.

The Five Negative Attributes and Qidam
Commentator defines negative attributes and explains qidam as negation of beginning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of qidam (eternity) as a negative attribute of Allah, its meaning as the negation of beginning, and the distinction from the philosophers' notion of eternity by another.

Core Idea
Qidam is not 'older than everything'; it is the absolute negation of any beginning.

This lesson introduces the five negative attributes that safeguard Allah's transcendence. It begins with qidam, which establishes that Allah is eternal by His essence, not through any cause. Understanding this concept is crucial because it immediately separates Islamic theology from the philosophers' claim that the world is eternal from God.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the continuous Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the flow from the matn line to the commentary.
The passage includes a footnote, which is part of the source.
2
Identify the key definitions
Find where the commentator defines 'negative attributes' and what he says about their function. Then locate the definition of qidam.
Negative attributes negate what is not befitting Allah.
3
Understand qidam as salb al-awwaliyyah
The commentator explicitly states that the meaning of qidam is the negation of beginning. Reflect on why this is a negative attribute.
It is not a positive affirmation of age but a negation.
4
Learn the warning against qidam bil-ghayr
Note the commentator's warning not to confuse Allah's qidam with the philosophers' concept of eternal world through another. Read the footnote for the refutation.
The proof: if He were not eternal, He would be originated.
5
Try the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to test your understanding of qidam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهْيَ القِدَمُ بِالذَّاتِ فَاعْلَمْ والبَقَا * قِيامُهُ بِنَفْسِهِ، يَلْتَ التَّقَى

شرح الشيخ حسن محمد المشاط المكي المالكي:
الصفات السلبية | ثم تليها) في الذكر صفات (خمسة سلبية)، لأن مدلول كلّ واحد من الخمسة سلب ونفي ما لا يليق بالذات العلية، كما سيأتي. (وهي) أي: السلبية القدم بالذات) أي: إن الله تعالى قديم لذاته، أي: لا لِعِلّة اقتضت وجوده، تعالى عن ذلك، ومعنى القدم: سلب الأولية، وأن الله تعالى لا أولية لوجوده، فاعلم) ذلك، ولا تقل بالقدم القدم المقابل بالغير (١).

(١) وهو قول الفلاسفة، فإنهم قالوا: إن العالم قديم، وقدمه بالغير، ومرادهم بالغير وجوده تعالى فطابقونا على أن القدم الذاتي لا يكون إلا لله تعالى وخالفونا في قولهم بقدم العالم، ويسمونه: قدما بالغير، ونحن نقول بحدوثه. والدليل على قدمه تعالى: أنه لو لم يكن قديمًا لكان حادثا - تعالى الله عن =
And they are: eternity by essence, so know, and everlastingness, and His self-subsistence, it follows piety. Commentary by Sheikh Hasan Muhammad al-Mashat al-Maliki: The negative attributes: Then after it) in mention are five negative attributes, because the implication of each of the five is negation and denial of what is not befitting the Exalted Essence, as will come. (And they are) i.e., the negative: eternity by essence) meaning: Allah, exalted, is eternal by His essence, i.e., not due to a cause that necessitated His existence, exalted above that. The meaning of eternity is the negation of beginning, and that Allah has no beginning to His existence. Know that, and do not say 'eternity' as the eternity contrasted with the other. (1) It is the saying of the philosophers, for they said: the world is eternal, and its eternity is by other, and they mean by 'other' His existence, exalted. So they agreed with us that self-subsistent eternity is only for Allah, but they disagreed with us in their saying that the world is eternal, and they call it: eternity by other. We say it is originated. The proof of His eternity is that if He were not eternal, He would be originated - exalted is Allah from =
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage introduces the five negative (salbiyyah) attributes and explains the first one: qidam (eternality). The commentator quotes the matn lines that list the first two salbiyyah attributes, then explains that these attributes negate what is not befitting Allah. He then focuses on qidam: Allah is eternal by His essence, not by a cause. The meaning of qidam is the negation of any beginning (salb al-awwaliyyah). He warns against the concept of 'qidam bil-ghayr' (eternity by another) held by philosophers who claim the world is eternal through God. The footnote gives a brief refutation: if Allah were not eternal, He would be originated, which is impossible.

القدم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qidam means Allah existed before everything else in time, similar to being extremely old.
Correction: Qidam is not about temporal priority; it is the negation of any beginning. It means Allah's existence has no starting point, not that He is simply older than creation.

B) Negation of beginning
C) Self-subsistence
D) Everlastingness

Key Takeaway
Qidam is a negative attribute that affirms Allah's eternal existence by negating any beginning to His existence.

?

?
If Allah were not eternal, He would be originated — and that is impossible. Does this logical certainty settle in your heart, or do you find yourself doubting? What would it mean for your entire worldview if the foundation of Allah's eternity wavered?

Understanding the Nafsiyyah Attribute
Mashāt defines the nafsiyyah attribute and explains its meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the nafsiyyah attribute and how it differs from attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī).

Core Idea
The nafsiyyah attribute describes the essence itself without any added meaning.

In this passage, Mulla ʿAlī al-Qārī introduces a key category of divine attributes: the nafsiyyah attribute. He explains that this attribute is so essential that the divine essence cannot be conceived without it, yet it does not add any extra meaning to the essence. Understanding this helps distinguish the nafsiyyah from other positive attributes that do imply additional meanings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the definition and the contrasting examples.
Notice the verse line at the start; it's a poetic summary.
2
Identify the key definition
Find the sentence that defines the nafsiyyah attribute. Note that it is a positive (thubūtiyya) attribute that indicates the essence itself.
The definition uses 'صفة ثبوتية' and 'يدل على نفس الذات'.
3
Understand the contrast
See how the author excludes attributes of meanings (like power). Contrast the nafsiyyah with those attributes that indicate an extra meaning beyond the essence.
The phrase 'وخرج صفات المعاني' signals the exclusion.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this distinction matters in theology. The nafsiyyah attribute (existence) is inseparable from God's essence, unlike other attributes that are additional in meaning.
This is a foundational concept in ʿilm al-kalām.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذي تسمى صفة نفسية * ثم تليها خمسة سلبية
الصفة النفسية (وذي) أي وهذه الصفة، وهي صفة الوجود، (تسمى: صفة نفسية منسوبة إلى النفس أي الذات، ومعناها: الصفة التي لا تُعقَلُ الذات بدونها.
وتُعرَّف بأنها: صفة ثبوتية، يدل الوصف بها على نفس الذات أي: لا على معنى زائد على الذات.
وخرج صفات المعاني نحو القدرة، والمعنوية، فإن الوصف بهما يدل على معنى زائد على الذات، ولا يدل الوصف على نفس الذات.
And this is called a nafsiyyah attribute * then follow it five negative ones. The nafsiyyah attribute: (and this) i.e., this attribute, which is the attribute of existence, (is called: a nafsiyyah attribute, attributed to the self i.e., the essence, and its meaning: the attribute without which the essence is not understood. And it is defined as: a positive attribute, the description by which indicates the essence itself, i.e., not an extra meaning upon the essence. And it excludes the attributes of meanings like power and the virtual attributes, for the description by them indicates an extra meaning upon the essence, and the description does not indicate the essence itself.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage defines the nafsiyyah attribute, which is the attribute of existence. The author first quotes the line from the poem: 'And this is called a nafsiyyah attribute, then follow it five negative ones.' Then he explains: the nafsiyyah attribute is called 'nafsiyyah' because it is attributed to the essence (nafs/self); its meaning is that the essence cannot be conceived without it. It is defined as a positive attribute whose description indicates the essence itself without any additional meaning. He then contrasts this with the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma'ānī) such as power, and the virtual attributes (al-ma'nawiyya), which indicate an extra meaning beyond the essence and do not directly indicate the essence itself. Thus, the nafsiyyah attribute uniquely signifies the essence per se.

Key Terms
الصفة النفسية
صفة الثبوتية
صفات المعاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the nafsiyyah attribute is merely a mental concept, but it is a real attribute inseparable from the essence.
Correction: The passage clarifies that it is a positive attribute (thubūtiyya) that indicates the essence itself, not a mere mental construct.

Checkpoint

A) It indicates an extra meaning beyond the essence.
B) It indicates the essence itself without any extra meaning.
C) It indicates the actions of God.
D) It indicates the negation of imperfection.

Key Takeaway
The nafsiyyah attribute is a positive attribute that directly indicates the divine essence without any added meaning, distinguishing it from other attributes like power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you affirm that Allah exists, do you truly believe that His existence is His very essence, or do you unconsciously imagine it as a separate quality? How does this distinction impact the intimacy of your relationship with Him?
?
If the nafsiyyah attribute indicates Allah's essence directly without any added concept, what does that say about your attempts to 'define' Allah with your own mental images? Are you willing to surrender your imagination to the precise definitions of the scholars?
?
The nafsiyyah attribute is positive yet does not add meaning. Does your heart find rest in knowing that Allah is known through a positive attribute, or does it struggle with the idea that His essence is not something you can fully grasp? Will you commit to deepening your understanding of Allah's attributes as taught by Ahl al-Sunna?

The First Negative Attribute: Eternality (al-Qidam)
Mashāt introduces the five negative attributes and explains the first: al-qidam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of negative attributes, particularly al-qidam, and how it differs from the philosophers' concept of eternity by another.

Core Idea
God's eternity means He has no beginning—not that He is old.

Sanusi introduces the five negative attributes that negate what is unworthy of God. The first is al-qidam: God is eternal by His own essence, not borrowed from anything. This lesson defines qidam and clarifies the Islamic stance against the philosophers' claim that the world is eternal by another.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening on negative attributes
Notice that the author introduces five negative attributes as a group and explains they negate what is not befitting Allah.
This sets the context for all five.
2
Find the definition of al-qidam
Identify how the author defines qidam: as the negation of beginning (salb al-awwaliyya) and that Allah is eternal by Himself, not due to any cause.
3
Understand the warning against philosophical error
Read the footnote carefully. It contrasts the Islamic concept of essential eternity (qidam bi al-dhat) with the philosophers' concept of eternity by another (qidam bil-ghayr).
The philosophers claim the world is eternal through God, but Muslims affirm only God's essential eternity.
4
Review the proof for qidam
The passage ends with a short proof: if Allah were not eternal, He would be originated. Reflect on why this must be false.
This is a simple argument from impossibility of the opposite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تليها) في الذكر صفات (خمسة سلبية)، لأن مدلول كلّ واحد من الخمسة سلب ونفي ما لا يليق بالذات العلية، كما سيأتي.
وهي أي: السلبية القدم بالذات أي: إن الله تعالى قديم لذاته، أي: لا لِعِلّة اقتضت وجوده، تعالى عن ذلك، ومعنى القدم: سلب الأولية، وأن الله تعالى لا أولية لوجوده، فاعلم ذلك، ولا تقل بالقدم القدم المقابل بالغير (١).
(١) وهو قول الفلاسفة، فإنهم قالوا: إن العالم قديم، وقدمه بالغير، ومرادهم بالغير وجوده تعالى فطابقونا على أن القدم الذاتي لا يكون إلا لله تعالى وخالفونا في قولهم بقدم العالم، ويسمونه: قدما بالغير، ونحن نقول بحدوثه. والدليل على قدمه تعالى: أنه لو لم يكن قديمًا لكان حادثا - تعالى الله عن =
Then follow it in mention five negative attributes, because the significance of each of the five is the negation and denial of what is not befitting the most high essence, as will come. And they, i.e., the negative ones (are): al-qidam bi al-dhat, meaning that Allah, exalted, is eternal by Himself, i.e., not due to a cause that necessitated His existence, exalted is He above that. And the meaning of qidam is the negation of precedence, and that Allah, exalted, has no beginning to His existence. So know that, and do not say qidam [in the sense of] the qidam that is opposite to [the one] by another. (1) And it is the saying of the philosophers, for they said: The world is eternal, and its eternity is by another, and they mean by 'another' His existence, exalted. So they agreed with us that essential eternity is only for Allah, but they disagreed with us in their claim that the world is eternal, and they call it: eternity by another. And we say it is originated. And the proof for His eternity is that if He were not eternal, He would be originated – exalted is Allah above =
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage introduces the five negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyya), which negate what is unbecoming of God. It then explains the first negative attribute: al-qidam (eternality). Qidam is defined as the negation of beginning (salb al-awwaliyya); God is eternal by His essence, not due to any cause. The author warns against confusing this with the philosophers' concept of 'eternity by another' (qidam bil-ghayr), which they apply to the world. The footnote elaborates: the philosophers claim the world is eternal by virtue of God, but Muslims affirm essential eternity for God alone and the world's temporality. A brief proof is given: if God were not eternal, He would be originated.

Key Terms
الصفات السلبية
القدم
القدم بالذات
القدم بالغير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that 'qadīm' means simply 'old' or that the philosophers' claim of the world's eternity is compatible with Islam.
Correction: Qidam means without beginning, not just old. The philosophers' eternity by another is rejected because only Allah has essential eternity.

Checkpoint
What does the attribute of al-qidam negate?
A) It negates the need for a cause.
B) It negates any beginning of existence.
C) It negates similarity to creation.
D) It negates the possibility of non-existence.

Key Takeaway
God's attribute of eternality (al-qidam) means He has no beginning, a negation that only applies to Him essentially.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever act as if God began or as if He is old? This week, when you pray, take a moment to reflect: 'Allah was before everything, and He never began.' How does that change your awe of Him? Will you commit to starting each day with this reflection?
?
The philosophers saw the world as eternal by God. In your daily life, do you treat something as permanent like the Creator? Identify one thing you rely on as if it will never end. What action can you take today to shift that reliance solely to Allah?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's existence has no cause, would you still seek security in secondary causes? Where in your life do you fear losing what you think sustains you? Will you make a concrete du'a this week asking Allah to be your only sustainer?

The Attribute of Everlastingness (al-Baqā')
Mashāt defines baqā' and gives a proof based on pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of God's attribute of everlastingness (baqā') and the rational proof that whatever is eternal cannot cease to exist.

Core Idea
God's existence has no end because His beginninglessness precludes ending.

The second negative attribute discussed by Mashāt is baqā', or everlastingness. This attribute negates the possibility of ending for Allah. In this lesson, we examine the precise meaning of baqā' and the concise logical proof that establishes it from the attribute of pre-eternity (qidam).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation to grasp the definition and proof of baqā'.
Notice that the proof builds on the attribute of pre-eternity.
2
Identify the definition of baqā'
Baqā' is defined as negation of ending (salb al-ākharīyah). Understand that it means God's existence has no end.
3
Understand the logical proof
The proof states that if something is established as eternal (qadīm), its nonexistence is impossible. Reflect on why this follows.
If it were possible, it would need a preponderator and become originated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) ثاني الصفات السلبية: (البقا)ء وهو سلب الآخرية، أي أنه تعالى لا آخر لوجوده، لأن ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه(۱).
وثالث الصفات السلبية: (قيامه تعالى (بنفسه) بمعنى: أنه تعالى لا يحتاج إلى محل ولا إلى مخصص، أي: فاعل، وقد أشار بعضهم إلى ذلك وإلى دليله فقال:
فَإِنْ يَقُولُوا هَلْ لِرَبِنَا مَكَان * فَاللَّهُ قَبْلَ خَلْقِهِ المَكَان كَان
لَو كَانَ رَبُّنَا القَدِيمِ في مَكَان • لَكَان مُحْتَاجًا إِلَى ذَاك المَكَان
ثُمَّ إِذَا احْتَاجَ لَهُ قَدْ افْتَقَر * لِحَادِثِ وَهُوَ قَدِيمَ اسْتَقَر
ثم دعا الناظم رحمه الله تعالى للقارئ بقوله: (نلت التقى)، وهي من التقوى: امتثال المأمورات واجتناب المنهيات، وهي المرتبة الوسطى المشار إليها بقوله:
خَلَّ الذُّنُوبَ صَغِيرَها وكَبِيرَها فَهو التَّقى واصْنَع كَمَاشِ فَوقَ أَرْ * ضِ الشَّوكِ يَحذَرُ ما يَرَى لَا تَحْقِرَنَّ صَغِيرَة * إنَّ الجِبَالَ مِنَ الحَصَى
ثم أشار إلى رابع الصفات السلبية بقوله: (مخالف للغير) معطوف على ذلك، فيلزم إفتقاره إلى محدث، ثم محدثه كذلك لانعقاد التماثل بينهما، وهو مفض إلى الدور أو التسلسل، وكلاهما محال، فما أديا إليه وهو الحدوث محال.
(۱) والدليل على بقائه تعالى : أن ما ثبت قِدَمُه استحال عدمه، وإلا لجاز عليه العدم فيحتاج إلى مُرَجّح، فيكون حادثًا لا قديمًا، كيف وقد ثَبَتَ قدمه.
And (the) second of the negative attributes: al-baqā', which is the negation of ending, i.e., He, exalted, has no end to His existence, because that whose eternality is established, its nonexistence is impossible. (1) And the third of the negative attributes: His, exalted, self-subsistence (qiyāmuhu bi nafsihi), meaning that He, exalted, does not need a place nor a specifier, i.e., an agent. And some have alluded to that and its proof, saying: 'If they say, does our Lord have a place? * God was before the creation of place. If our Lord, the Eternal, were in a place * He would need that place. Then if He needed it, He would be in need * of an originated thing, while He is Eternal, settled.' Then the versifier asked for mercy for the reader by his saying: (you attained piety), and it is from taqwā: performing the commanded and avoiding the forbidden, and it is the middle rank alluded to in his saying: 'Leave sins, small and large, that is piety. And act like one walking above a thorny ground, cautious of what he sees. Do not belittle a small sin, for mountains are from pebbles.' Then he pointed to the fourth negative attribute by his saying: (distinct from other), coordinated with that, so it necessarily follows its need for an originator, then its originator likewise because of the similarity between them, and that leads to vicious circle or infinite regress, both of which are impossible, so what they lead to, which is origination, is impossible. (1) And the proof for His everlastingness: that whose eternality is established, its nonexistence is impossible; otherwise nonexistence would be possible for it, so it would need a preponderator, and then it would be originated, not eternal – how [could that be] when its eternality has been established?
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage covers three negative attributes: baqā' (everlastingness), qiyām bi nafsih (self-subsistence), and mukhālif lil-ghayr (distinct from other). For baqā', it is defined as the negation of ending; a brief proof is given: if something is eternal, its nonexistence is impossible. For qiyām bi nafsih, it means God does not need a place or a specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ); a poetic proof is cited: if God were in a place, He would need that place, and since He is eternal, He cannot be in need of an originated thing. Then the author explains the prayer 'nilt al-tuqā' and defines taqwā as performing commands and avoiding prohibitions, the middle path. Finally, he discusses mukhālif lil-ghayr: God's distinctness from all others; a proof is given that if something were similar to God, it would also need an originator, leading to vicious circle or infinite regress, so the world must be originated.

Key Terms
البقاء
الآخرية
القدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's everlastingness is simply a statement of fact without logical necessity.
Correction: The text shows it is logically necessary: if God is eternal in the past, He must be eternal in the future; otherwise, He would be contingent.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the proof given for the attribute of baqā' (everlastingness)?
A) If God were not everlasting, He would need a place.
B) Whatever is eternal cannot become nonexistent.
C) The world is originated, so God must be everlasting.
D) The poets have testified to it.

Key Takeaway
Everlastingness (baqā') is a necessary consequence of pre-eternity: if God has no beginning, He can have no end.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your life before Allah has no end—that your actions here will echo forever—would you change anything about how you live this moment? What precisely, and why haven't you changed it yet?
?
The pre-eternal God cannot cease to exist. Your existence, by contrast, is a borrowed breath. How does the certainty of an everlasting Judge reshape the weight you give to fleeting pleasures today?
?
You know that God is the Last, that everything perishes except His face. If your worldly pursuits will be ashes, what remains of your life that will survive into that everlasting presence? Name one thing—and commit to building it today.

The Attribute of Self-Subsistence (Qiyām bi Nafsih)
Mashāt defines qiyām bi nafsih and cites a poetic proof, followed by a prayer for piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of God's self-subsistence (qiyām bi nafsih) and the poetic proof that He does not need any place or specifier.

Core Idea
God does not need a place or cause; He is self-subsistent and independent of all creation.

The third negative attribute is qiyām bi nafsih, meaning that Allah subsists by Himself without needing a place (makān) or a specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ). Mashāt presents a poem that beautifully illustrates the absurdity of God being confined in space. The passage also includes a prayer for the reader to attain taqwā (piety), which is defined as obeying commands and avoiding prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and the poem
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the definition of qiyām bi nafsih and the poem that proves it.
The poem uses a logical argument: if God were in a place, He would need that place, contradicting His eternity.
2
Understand the meaning of qiyām bi nafsih
It means God does not need a place (makān) nor a specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ) – an agent to determine His existence. He is self-sufficient.
This negates any dependence on created things.
3
Note the prayer and taqwā definition
The versifier prays for the reader to attain taqwā, which is defined as performing commands and avoiding prohibitions. Reflect on the connection to the main topic.
Taqwā is the middle path, as illustrated by the additional poetry.

?

?

The Attribute of Distinctness from Others (Mukhālif lil-Ghayr)
Mashāt defines mukhālif lil-ghayr and proves it by showing that similarity leads to absurd consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of God's attribute of being distinct from all others and the proof that similarity would lead to impossibility.

Core Idea
God is utterly unlike any creation; similarity would imply contingency and lead to an infinite regress.

The fourth negative attribute is mukhālif lil-ghayr, meaning that God is distinct from everything else. Mashāt gives a logical proof: if something were similar to God, it would also need an originator, leading to an infinite chain or a vicious circle, both impossible. This shows that the world must be originated and God is unique.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and the proof
Read the Arabic passage and translation, noting the definition of mukhālif lil-ghayr and the proof that follows.
The proof uses the concept of tamāthul (similarity) and its consequences.
2
Follow the logical argument
The argument: if something were similar to God, it would also need an originator; then that originator would need another, leading to infinite regress or circle—both impossible. Therefore, similarity is impossible, and God is distinct.
The impossibility of the conclusion proves the premise false.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that the world cannot be similar to God and must be originated (ḥādith). This reinforces God's uniqueness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What does the proof for mukhālif lil-ghayr (distinctness) involve?

D) The denial of multiple gods.

Key Takeaway
God is unique and distinct from all creation; any similarity would lead to an absurd infinite chain, so it is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself imagining God in human terms, such as thinking He feels anger or mercy exactly like a person does? What specific image of God do you need to actively reject after this lesson, and what will you replace it with?
?
If God were not utterly distinct from creation, He would be contingent like us—needing an originator. How does this truth deepen the reverence you feel when you say 'Allahu Akbar' (God is Greatest)? What will you do in your next prayer to remember this?
?
The proof shows that any similarity to God leads to logical absurdity. Is there a way you subtly treat God as if He is limited by human standards of justice or time? Commit to one concrete change in how you think about God’s actions in your life today.

Al-Baqa: The Eternal Endlessness of Allah
Defines al-baqa and provides its rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the negative attribute of al-baqa and its rational proof based on Allah's eternality.

Core Idea
If Allah is eternal without beginning, He must also be eternal without end.

In this lesson, we explore the second negative attribute: al-baqa, which negates any end to Allah's existence. The author provides a concise rational argument: if something is eternal, its nonexistence is impossible. This attribute complements al-qidam and completes our understanding of Allah's timeless existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-Baqa
Read the Arabic definition carefully: 'al-baqa is the negation of otherness (al-akhariyyah), meaning no end to His existence.' Note that it is a negative attribute.
Contrast with positive attributes like knowledge or power.
2
Understand the proof from Qidam
The proof states that whatever is eternal (qadim) cannot cease to exist, because if it could, it would need a preponderant and would be contingent. This establishes baqa as necessary.
The logic is: if possible, it would require a cause, contradicting qidam.
3
Reflect on the necessity of Baqa
Consider why baqa must be a real distinct attribute: it is the logical consequence of qidam. Allah's existence has no temporal boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) ثاني الصفات السلبية: (البقا)ء وهو سلب الآخرية، أي أنه تعالى لا آخر لوجوده، لأن ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه. وثالث الصفات السلبية: (قيامه تعالى (بنفسه) بمعنى: أنه تعالى لا يحتاج إلى محل ولا إلى مخصص، أي: فاعل، وقد أشار بعضهم إلى ذلك وإلى دليله فقال: فإن يقولوا هل لربنا مكان * فالله قبل خلقه المكان كان لو كان ربنا القديم في مكان • لكان محتاجا إلى ذاك المكان ثم إذا احتاج له قد افتقر لحادث وهو قديم استقر ثم دعا الناظم رحمه الله تعالى للقارئ بقوله: (نلت التقى)، وهي من التقوى: امتثال المأمورات واجتناب المنهيات، وهي المرتبة الوسطى المشار إليها بقوله: خل الذنوب صغيرها وكبيرها فهو التقى واصنع كماش فوق أرض الشوك يحذر ما يرى لا تحقرن صغيرة إن الجبال من الحصى والدليل على بقائه تعالى: أن ما ثبت قِدَمُه استحال عدمه، وإلا لجاز عليه العدم فيحتاج إلى مُرَجّح، فيكون حادثًا لا قديمًا، كيف وقد ثَبَتَ قدمه.
(And) the second of the negative attributes: (al-baqa'), which is the negation of otherness, i.e., that He, exalted, has no end to His existence, because whatever has been established as eternal, its non-existence is impossible. And the third of the negative attributes: (His, exalted, being self-subsistent), meaning that He, exalted, does not need a locus nor a particularizer, i.e., an agent. And some have alluded to this and to its proof, saying: 'If they say: Does our Lord have a place? So Allah before creating place was. If our eternal Lord were in a place, He would be in need of that place. Then if He needs it, He would be dependent on a contingent, while He is eternal and established.' Then the poet, may Allah have mercy on him, called upon the reader by his saying: 'You have attained piety (nalta al-tuqa),' which is from taqwa: compliance with commands and avoidance of prohibitions, and it is the middle rank referred to by his saying: 'Leave sins, small and large, for that is taqwa, and act like one walking over thorny ground, cautious of what he sees. Do not belittle a small sin, for mountains are made of pebbles.' And the proof of His, exalted, enduring eternity is: that whatever has been established as eternal, its non-existence is impossible; otherwise non-existence would be possible for it, so it would need a preponderant, and thus it would be contingent, not eternal, given that its eternity has been established.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines two negative attributes: al-baqa' (eternity a parte post) and qiyamuhu bi nafsihi (self-subsistence). The author begins with al-baqa', explaining that it negates any end to God's existence, and gives the rational proof: whatever is eternal cannot cease to exist. Then he defines qiyamuhu bi nafsihi, meaning God does not need a substrate or a creator. A supporting poem is cited to show that God existed before place, so cannot be in need of place. Then the author comments on the poet's invocation 'nalta al-tuqa' (you have attained piety), defining taqwa as obedience and caution. Finally, the proof for al-baqa' is repeated in a more formal manner: if God were not eternal, He would need a preponderant and be contingent, contradiction.

Key Terms
البقاء
الآخرية
القدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that baqa means Allah persists through time, but it actually negates an end entirely.
Correction: Baqa is a negative attribute, not a positive one: it denies the possibility of cessation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of al-baqa?
A) Negation of beginning
B) Negation of ending
C) Self-subsistence
D) Difference from others

Key Takeaway
Al-baqa is the logical corollary of Allah's eternality: what has no beginning cannot have an end.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah will never cease to exist, how would that change your attachment to temporary things like wealth, status, or relationships? What is one temporary thing you can consciously detach from today?
?
How does the certainty of Allah's eternal existence confront your fear of death or loss? Since your own existence is temporary, what eternal investment can you make right now that will outlast you?
?
Since Allah has no end, your relationship with Him is the only thing that lasts. What have you done today to strengthen that relationship, and what will you do tomorrow to ensure it grows?

Qiyamuhu bi Nafsihi: Allah's Self-Subsistence
Defines qiyamuhu bi nafsihi with a poetic proof and taqwa exhortation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the attribute of qiyamuhu bi nafsihi and its proof through the poem about place.

Core Idea
Allah does not need a place or a creator—He is self-subsistent.

The third negative attribute is qiyamuhu bi nafsihi, meaning Allah is independent of any locus or particularizer. The author cites a poetic proof that God existed before creation, so cannot require a place. The poem also includes a call to taqwa, reinforcing the relevance of theology to practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of Qiyamuhu bi Nafsihi
Read the Arabic definition: 'He does not need a locus (mahall) nor a particularizer (mukhassis), i.e., an agent.' Note that it negates two things: need for a substrate and need for a cause.
Contrast with created beings that require a place and a creator.
2
Analyze the poetic proof
The poem argues from God's existence before creation: if someone asks 'Does our Lord have a place?' the answer is that Allah existed before place, so He cannot be in need of it. Needing a place would make Him dependent on a contingent, contradicting His eternality.
The poem is a concise demonstration using temporal priority.
3
Understand the Taqwa commentary
The poet prays for the reader's piety (taqwa), defined as obeying commands and avoiding prohibitions. He emphasizes not belittling small sins, using the metaphor of mountains formed from pebbles.
This connects theological knowledge to moral action.
4
Reflect on the relationship between attribute and practice
Consider how recognizing Allah's self-subsistence leads to humility and piety: He is not dependent on anything, so we must depend on Him alone.

?

?
If Allah is completely self-sufficient and needs nothing from you, then why do you sometimes act as if your worship is doing Him a favor? How can you shift your mindset to see worship as your own desperate need for Him?

The Fourth Negative Attribute: Mukhalafah lil-Ghayr
Defines mukhalafah lil-ghayr and gives a rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning and rational proof of the attribute 'Mukhalafah lil-Ghayr' (God's difference from all contingent things).

Core Idea
If God were like His creation, He would need a creator — so He must be utterly different.

This lesson introduces the fourth negative attribute: Allah's complete difference from all contingent beings. Al-Kharida and its commentator Sanusi argue that affirming similarity would lead to impossibility, so transcendence is necessary. We will explore the meaning of this attribute and its logical foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to get a sense of the argument.
The passage combines definition and proof in a concise style.
2
Understand the definition of mukhalafah
Notice what the attribute negates: God is not a body, accident, moving, stationary, etc. He is different in essence, attributes, and actions.
This is a negative attribute — it removes similarity without affirming a positive quality.
3
Follow the rational proof
The proof is a reductio: if God were similar to contingent things, He would also be contingent and dependent, leading to circularity or infinite regress — both impossible. Therefore, similarity is impossible.
The argument assumes the principle that similar things share the same ontological status.
4
Reflect on the implication
Reflect on why this attribute is necessary to believe. It protects tawhid by affirming that nothing resembles Allah in any way.
This connects to the broader Islamic creed of transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أشار إلى رابع الصفات السلبية بقوله: (مخالف للغير) معطوف على ذلك، فيلزم إفتقاره إلى محدث، ثم محدثه كذلك لانعقاد التماثل بينهما، وهو مفض إلى الدور أو التسلسل، وكلاهما محال، فما أديا إليه وهو الحدوث محال. أي: ومخالفته تعالى لغيره من الحوادث، فليس هو تعالى بجسم، ولا عرض، ولا متحرك، ولا ساكن، إلى غير ذلك من صفات الحوادث. والمعنى أنه يجب لله تعالى مخالفته للحوادث في الذات والصفات والأفعال، ويجب على المكلف اعتقاد مخالفته للحوادث، لأنه لو كان مماثلًا لها لوجب له تعالى ما وجب لها من الحدوث والافتقار، وذلك محال. والدليل على مخالفته تعالى للغير: أنه لو كان مُمَائِلًا لها لوجب له تعالى ما وجب لها من الحدوث والافتقار، وذلك محال.
Then he alluded to the fourth of the negative attributes by his saying: (Different from others) coordinated with that, so its dependence on an originator would follow, then its originator likewise due to the conception of similarity between them, which leads to circularity or infinite regress, both of which are impossible, so what they lead to, namely contingency, is impossible. Meaning: His, exalted, being different from others among contingent things; so He, exalted, is not a body, nor an accident, nor moving, nor stationary, and so on from the attributes of contingent things. The meaning is that it is necessary for Allah, exalted, to be different from contingent things in essence, attributes, and actions, and it is obligatory for the accountable person to believe in His difference from contingent things, because if He were similar to them, then what is necessary for them, namely contingency and dependence, would be necessary for Him, exalted, and that is impossible. And the proof of His, exalted, difference from others: that if He were similar to them, then what is necessary for them would be necessary for Him, exalted, of contingency and dependence, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth negative attribute: mukhalafah lil-ghayr (difference from others). The author argues that if God were similar to contingent beings, then He would require a creator, leading to circularity or infinite regress—both impossible—so contingency is impossible. Then he clarifies the meaning: God is not a body, accident, etc. It is necessary for God to be unlike creation in essence, attributes, and actions, and it is obligatory for believers to affirm this. The proof is that similarity would imply the same dependence and contingency as creation, which is impossible.

Key Terms

الحوادث
التماثل
الدور
التسلسل
الحدوث
الافتقار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God is different only in some attributes but similar in others.
Correction: The attribute means total difference in essence, attributes, and actions; any similarity would imply contingency, which is impossible for God.

Checkpoint
What does the proof for mukhalafah establish?
A) God is similar to creation
B) God is unlike creation in essence only
C) If God were similar to creation, He would be contingent
D) God is a body

Key Takeaway
Allah is absolutely unlike any created thing; any similarity would necessitate contingency, which is impossible for the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allahu Akbar', do you truly feel that He is beyond any comparison, or does your mind subtly create an image of Him? What step will you take today to purify your tawheed from any trace of tamathul?
?
The passage proves that even one shared attribute between Allah and creation would lead to absurdity. Examine your heart: do you ever think of Allah's mercy or power as being like a human's but greater? How will you actively replace such thoughts with the understanding that His attributes are entirely different?
?
If Allah were like His creation, He would need a creator. How does this truth reshape your awareness of your own dependence on Him? Write one concrete way you will live this week with deeper gratitude for His absolute uniqueness.

Understanding Wahdaniyyah: Oneness in Essence, Attributes, and Actions
Defines wahdaniyyah and provides a Qur'anic proof for oneness of action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that wahdaniyyah negates multiplicity in God's essence, attributes, and actions, and why the Qur'anic proof of mutual prevention demonstrates the impossibility of multiple gods.

Core Idea
Oneness means no multiplicity in essence, attributes, or actions—only God truly acts.

This lesson introduces the fifth negative attribute: wahdaniyyah (oneness). Sanusi explains that this attribute negates any form of multiplicity in God's essence, attributes, and actions. The Qur'anic verse (21:22) provides a rational proof: if multiple gods existed, they would conflict, leading to cosmic ruin. Understanding oneness in this threefold way is essential for grasping tawhid in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three aspects of oneness
Carefully read the Arabic and translation to find where the author discusses essence, attributes, and actions. Note how each is defined.
The three aspects are explicitly listed.
2
Understand the negation of multiplicity
For each aspect, ask: what kind of multiplicity is being negated? For essence, it's composition or division; for attributes, it's separation; for actions, it's independent agency.
The negation is not just numerical but qualitative.
3
Examine the Qur'anic proof and the logic of mutual prevention
Read the verse and the summary of the proof. Understand the argument: multiple gods would lead to conflicting wills, causing corruption. Therefore, only one God can exist.
This is known as burhan al-tamani'.
4
Reflect on why wahdaniyyah is a negative attribute
Consider that negative attributes describe what God is not. Wahdaniyyah negates multiplicity, affirming absolute oneness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخامس الصفات السلبية: (وحدانية) وهي عبارة عن سلب الكثرة في الذات والصفات والأفعال، كما قال: (في الذات) أي: في ذاته تعالى اتصالا وانفصالا، أي: عدم الاثنينية في ذاته. أيضًا. (أو) أي: ووحدانيته في (صفاته تعالى (العلية) اتصالا وانفصالا ( والفعل) أي: وحدانيته تعالى في الفعل، أي: أنه متصف بوحدانية الأفعال، فليس ثَمَّ من له فعل من الأفعال سواه تعالى، قال الله تعالى: لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا وَالِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللهُ لَفَسَدَتَاً ) (٢). والآية تشير إلى برهان التمانع، وحاصله: أنه لو أمكن التعدد، لأمكن التمانع بينهما، بأن يريد أحدهما حركة زيدٍ مثلا، والآخرُ
And the fifth of the negative attributes: (Oneness), which is an expression of the negation of multiplicity in essence, attributes, and actions, as he said: (in essence) i.e., in His, exalted, essence, in terms of connectedness and separateness, i.e., the negation of duality in His essence. Also (or) i.e., His oneness (in His, exalted, high attributes) in terms of connectedness and separateness (and in action) i.e., His, exalted, oneness in action, meaning that He is characterized by oneness of actions, so there is no one who has any action besides Him, exalted. Allah, exalted, said: 'If there were in them other gods besides Allah, they would both be ruined' (21:22). And the verse alludes to the proof of mutual prevention, the summary of which is: if multiplicity were possible, then mutual prevention between them would be possible, such that one of them wills the movement of Zaid, for example, and the other
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth negative attribute: wahdaniyyah (oneness), which negates multiplicity in God's essence, attributes, and actions. In essence, it negates duality (e.g., composition or division). In attributes, it negates multiple distinct divine attributes that could be separated. In actions, it affirms that only God truly acts; others' actions are created by Him. The Qur'anic proof (21:22) is cited, arguing that multiple gods would lead to conflict and ruin. The author summarizes the proof of mutual prevention: if two gods existed, they could oppose each other, which would imply corruption of the universe.

Key Terms
الوحدانية
الكثرة
الذات
الصفات
الأفعال
التمانع
برهان التمانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Wahdaniyyah only means one in number, not unique in essence, attributes, and actions.
Correction: Wahdaniyyah negates any multiplicity in essence (no parts), attributes (no separate attributes), and actions (no independent actors besides God). It is a comprehensive oneness.

Checkpoint
The Qur'anic verse 21:22 is used to prove which attribute?
A) Qidam
B) Baqa
C) Wahdaniyyah
D) Mukhalafah

Key Takeaway
Wahdaniyyah is not merely numerical oneness but the absolute negation of any multiplicity or partner in God's essence, attributes, and actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that only Allah has the power to act, why do you still feel anxious about outcomes that depend on others? In what specific situation this week can you consciously attribute the result solely to Allah?
?
The proof of mutual prevention shows that multiple gods would cause chaos. Where in your own heart do you find conflicting 'gods'—like the desire for status, wealth, or comfort—that create inner turmoil? What is one step you can take today to submit those desires to Allah's oneness?
?
When you do a good deed, do you secretly feel that you produced it independently? Reflect on Allah's oneness in actions: your ability to pray or give was created by Him. How does this realization change the way you view your own achievements?

The Fifth Negative Attribute: Unity (Wahdaniyya)
Al-Mashat defines wahdaniyya and explains its three aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the fifth negative attribute wahdaniyya as the negation of multiplicity in Allah's essence, attributes, and actions.

Core Idea
Unity (wahdaniyya) negates all multiplicity in essence, attributes, and actions.

Al-Mashat now introduces the fifth negative attribute, which is central to tawhid. Understanding wahdaniyya goes beyond numerical oneness—it denies any form of multiplicity in Allah. This passage defines it and clarifies its three aspects, supported by a Qur'anic verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Pay attention to how Al-Mashat defines wahdaniyya and what it negates.
2
Identify the three aspects
The passage lists three domains where multiplicity is negated: essence (dhāt), attributes (ṣifāt), and actions (afʿāl). Find the specific phrases for each.
3
Understand the negation of multiplicity
Reflect on what 'negation of multiplicity' means in each domain. For essence, it means no composition or duality; for attributes, no multiplicity in perfect qualities; for actions, no other true agent besides Allah.
4
Examine the Qur'anic proof
Read the verse from Surah al-Anbiya (22) and consider how it supports the unity of action, showing that multiple gods would cause corruption.

Source Text

And the fifth of the negative attributes: (wahdaniyya) and it is an expression of the negation of multiplicity in the essence, attributes, and actions, as he said: (in the essence) i.e., in His essence, may He be exalted, in terms of conjunction and disjunction, i.e., the non-existence of duality in His essence. Also. Allah Almighty said: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would have been ruined' [Al-Anbiya 22].
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth negative attribute, wahdaniyya (unity), which negates multiplicity in three respects. The author first states the general meaning: negation of multiplicity in Allah's essence, attributes, and actions. Then he explains each: 'in the essence' means no composition or duality; 'in His attributes' means no multiplicity in His perfect attributes; 'in action' means that only Allah creates and causes actions—no other being has any true creative power. He cites the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Anbiya (22) as evidence for the unity of action, which is the foundation of the proof of mutual hindrance.

Correction: Wahdaniyya negates all forms of multiplicity, including composition, duality, and partnership, and it applies to essence, attributes, and actions.

The Supreme Importance of the Attribute of Tawhid
Al-Mashat quotes al-Sawi on the supreme importance of tawhid and a unique point about jinn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of tawhid is considered the most important divine attribute, how it relates to the naming of the science of tawhid, and the distinction between disbelief and shirk as illustrated by the jinn.

Core Idea
Tawhid is the most important divine attribute, central to Islamic theology.

Al-Mashat cites a short but profound passage from al-Sawi that highlights the preeminence of the attribute of tawhid. This attribute is so crucial that the entire field of Islamic theology is named after it. Moreover, al-Sawi makes an interesting observation about the jinn, which helps clarify the relationship between disbelief and shirk.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then read the literal English translation. Notice the structure: it begins with 'فائدة' indicating a beneficial point.
2
Identify the two main points
The passage makes two claims: first, the attribute of tawhid is the most important, hence the science is named after it; second, only some humans disbelieve in its opposite, while jinn do not commit shirk at all.
3
Reflect on why the science is named 'tawhid'
Consider why the study of Islamic theology is called 'ʿilm al-tawḥīd' (science of tawhid). This underscores that affirming Allah's oneness is the foundation of the faith.
This connects to the learning objective.
4
Understand the distinction between kufr and shirk
Al-Sawi notes that jinn can be disbelievers (kuffār) without committing shirk. This shows that disbelief and shirk are not identical.
This is a subtle but important point.

He then makes a striking observation: only some humans commit shirk by denying this attribute; the jinn collectively do not commit shirk, though they may disbelieve in other matters.

Proof for Negative Attributes
Poem and commentary prove God must have negative attributes to avoid contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for why God must possess five specific negative attributes to avoid the impossibility of contingency.

Core Idea
Negative attributes are logical necessities to prevent God's contingency.

The poem and commentary present a logical proof that God must be described with negative attributes. These are not arbitrary but rationally necessary to prevent the absurdity of God being contingent. Each attribute is defended by showing that its negation leads to an impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the poem and opening explanation
Start by reading the Arabic poem and its immediate commentary. Notice the conditional structure: if God were not described with these attributes, contingency would follow, which is impossible.
The phrase 'وَهوَ مُحَالٌ' (and it is impossible) is key.
2
Follow the proof for each attribute
The commentary elaborates on five negative attributes: pre-eternity, everlastingness, self-subsistence, dissimilarity to originated things, and unity. For each, it shows why God must possess them to avoid absurdity.
Each argument follows a similar logical pattern: if not X, then Y (contingency), which is impossible, so X is necessary.
3
Reflect on the overall conclusion
The passage ends by emphasizing that contingency upon God is impossible (محال) and that seeking uprightness is better than miracles. Consider how the proof establishes a rational foundation for these attributes.

If He were not described with them, then His contingency would be necessary, and it is impossible, so be upright. Then the poet, may the Lord cover him with His mercy, pointed to the proof of the negative attributes previously mentioned—the proof of the attributes—by his saying: (If He were not described, i.e., surely His being described, blessed and exalted, by the negative attributes is necessary, because if He were not described with them, His contingency would be necessary, and He is exalted from that. As for pre-eternity, it is apparent, for there is no intermediate between pre-eternity and contingency; so wherever contingency is negated, pre-eternity is established for Him. As for everlastingness, because if He were not described with them, He would not be pre-eternal; for one whose pre-eternity is established, his non-existence is impossible. As for self-subsistence, because if He subsisted by another, He would be an accident needing another for His subsistence, which is impossible. As for dissimilarity to originated things, because if He resembled any of them, He would be originated like them. As for unity, because if He had an equal or similar in His essence or attributes, incapacity would be necessary, and every incapable is originated, just as every originated is incapable, and contingency upon Him is impossible, as He said: (and it) i.e., contingency upon Him (is impossible) not admitting of logical existence. (So be upright) i.e., ask God for the path of uprightness, for it is better than a thousand miracles. And it is only that contingency upon Him is impossible.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for the negative attributes (الصفات السلبية) of God. It begins with the poem: 'If He were not described with them, then His contingency would be necessary, and it is impossible, so be upright.' The commentary explains that God must be described with negative attributes; otherwise, He would be contingent, which is impossible. The proof is then elaborated for each attribute: 1) Pre-eternity (القدم): If God were not eternal, He would be contingent; since contingency is negated, pre-eternity is affirmed. 2) Everlastingness (البقاء): If God were not described with it, He would not be pre-eternal, but pre-eternity necessitates impossibility of non-existence. 3) Self-subsistence (القيام بالنفس): If God subsisted by another, He would be an accident needing that other, which is impossible. 4) Dissimilarity to originated things (المخالفة للحوادث): If He resembled any created thing, He would be originated. 5) Unity (الوحدانية): If He had an equal, incapacity would result, and incapacity implies contingency, which is impossible for God. The passage concludes that contingency upon God is impossible and that seeking uprightness is better than miracles.

The Central Proof: Negative Attributes Prevent Huduth
Sanusi states the central conditional argument for negative attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core argument that God must possess negative attributes because their absence would entail temporal origination (huduth), which is impossible for God.

Core Idea
Without negative attributes, huduth follows; huduth is impossible, so attributes are necessary.

Sanusi presents a concise proof: if God were not described with the negative attributes, then huduth (temporal origination) would be necessary. But huduth is impossible for God, so the negative attributes are necessary. This lesson introduces this overarching argument and its logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening verse
Read the Arabic verse and its explanation. Notice the conditional structure: 'If He were not described with them, His temporal origination would follow, and it is impossible.'
The verse is a concise statement of the entire proof.
2
Understand the logical form
The argument is a modus tollens: if P (absence of attributes) then Q (huduth). Q is false (huduth is impossible), so P is false. Therefore, attributes are necessary.
3
See how qidam is derived
The commentator explains that negation of huduth directly affirms pre-eternity (qidam), because there is no intermediate between pre-eternity and temporal origination.
This connects to the negative attributes being necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ِلَوْ لَم يَكُنْ مُتَّصِفًا بِها لَزِمْ * حُدُوتُهُ وَهُوَ مُحالٌ فَاسْتَقِمْ | ۲۸
ثم أشار الناظم تغمده المولى برحمته إلى برهان السلبية المتقدمة دليل الصفات بقوله: (لو لم يكن أي: إنما وجب اتصافه تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى بالصفات السلبية، لأنه لو لم يكن متصفا بها لزم حدوثه تعالى وتنزه عن. القدم فظاهر، إذ لا واسطة بين القدم والحدوث، فحيث انتفى الحدوث ثبت له القدم.
وأما البقاء، فلأنه لو لم يكن متصفّا بها لم يكن قديما، فإن من ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه.
وأما القيام بالنفس، فلأنه لو قام بغيره لكان عرضًا محتاجًا في قيامه للغير، وهو محال.
وأما المخالفة للحوادث، فلأنه لو ماثل شيئًا منها لكان حادثا مثلها.
وأما الوحدانية، فلأنه لو كان له نظير ومثيل في ذاته أو صفاته، للزم العجز، وكل عاجز حادث، كما أن كل حادث عاجز، والحدوث عليه محال، كما قال: (وهو) أي: الحدوث عليه تعالى (محال) لا يقبل الثبوت عقلا، (فاستقم) أي: اطلب من الله تعالى طريق الاستقامة، فإنها خير من ألف كرامة.

التسلسل والدورا إذا استمر العدد إلى ما لا نهاية له، لأن التسلسل: هو ترتب أمور غير متناهية، وهو محال.

If He were not described with them, His temporal origination (huduth) would follow, and it is impossible, so remain upright. | 28. Then the versifier, may the Lord envelop him in His mercy, indicated the aforementioned proof of the negative attributes—the proof of the attributes—by his saying: (If He were not described with them, i.e., it is only necessary that He, Blessed and Exalted, be described with the negative attributes, because if He were not described with them, His temporal origination (huduth) would be necessary, and by His exaltedness He is free from that. As for pre-eternity (qidam), it is obvious, for there is no intermediate between pre-eternity and temporal origination; so wherever temporal origination is negated, pre-eternity is affirmed for Him. As for everlastingness (baqa'), because if He were not described with it, He would not be pre-eternal; for whoever's pre-eternity is established, His non-existence is impossible. As for self-subsistence (qiyam bi nafsihi), because if He subsisted through another, He would be an accident (arad) needing another for His subsistence, which is impossible. As for being unlike originated things (mukhalafat al-hawadith), because if He resembled any of them, He would be originated like them. As for oneness (wahdaniyya), because if He had a peer or likeness in His essence or attributes, incapacity ('ajz) would follow, and every incapable being is originated, just as every originated being is incapable, and temporal origination is impossible for Him, as He said: (And it) i.e., temporal origination for Him, Exalted, (is impossible) not rationally acceptable, (so remain upright) i.e., ask Allah for the path of rectitude, for it is better than a thousand miracles. And temporal origination is only impossible for Him, Exalted, because it leads to infinite regress) from afda yufdi, i.e., leads and arrives at infinite regress (tasalsul) and circularity (dawr) if the number continues without end, for tasalsul is the arrangement of non-finite things, and it is impossible. (And dawr) i.e., it leads to dawr—with a fat-ha on the emphasized dal—if it does not continue, because the meaning of dawr is the dependence of something on that which depends on that same thing from one aspect, and it is impossible, as he said: (And it is the clear impossibility) i.e., the evident one that does not need proof.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessity of God's negative attributes. The versifier (Sanusi) states in line 28 that if God were not described with these attributes, then temporal origination (huduth) would follow, and huduth is impossible for God. The commentator explains each of the five negative attributes: pre-eternity (qidam), everlastingness (baqa'), self-subsistence (qiyam bi nafsihi), being unlike originated things (mukhalafat al-hawadith), and oneness (wahdaniyya). For each, he shows that the lack of the attribute would entail huduth, which is impossible. Then he explains why huduth is impossible: because it would lead to either infinite regress (tasalsul) or circularity (dawr), both of which are rationally impossible. The argument is that if God were originated, then His existence would be dependent on a prior cause, leading to an infinite chain (tasalsul) if that causal sequence extended endlessly, or to circular dependence (dawr) if the causal chain eventually looped back. Both are absurd. Thus, huduth is impossible for God, and therefore He must possess the negative attributes that negate any possibility of huduth.

Key Terms
سلوبية
حدوث
قدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'negative attributes' are purely negative without affirming anything positive.
Correction: In fact, they necessarily imply positive attributes like qidam (pre-eternity).

Checkpoint
What is the logical structure of Sanusi's argument for negative attributes?
A) If P then Q, Q is true, so P is true
B) If P then Q, Q is false, so P is false
C) If not P then not Q, not Q is true, so not P is false
D) P or Q, not P, so Q

Key Takeaway
The necessity of negative attributes is derived from the impossibility of huduth for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever unconsciously imagine God as having some temporal limitation, even though this lesson proves such a thought would imply huduth? How can you actively rid your mind of such anthropomorphic traces?
?
The commentator insists there is no middle ground between pre-eternity and temporal origination. Is your certainty about God's attributes, like His being al-Awwal (the First), absolute, or do you sometimes treat it as a vague belief? What would it look like to live with unwavering conviction in this truth?
?
If God’s pre-eternity demands negative attributes, which in turn safeguard His perfection, what does that mean for your worship? Are you approaching Him as the necessarily pre-eternal and perfect Being, or as a being subject to your own finite concepts? Repent and rectify your understanding.

The Five Negative Attributes and Their Proofs
Sanusi enumerates five negative attributes with individual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how each of the five negative attributes (qidam, baqa', qiyam bi nafsihi, mukhalafat al-hawadith, wahdaniyya) is proven by showing that its absence would entail huduth.

Core Idea
Each negative attribute is proven by showing its opposite leads to huduth.

Sanusi enumerates five negative attributes and provides a brief proof for each. For every attribute, he argues that if God lacked it, huduth would follow. This lesson examines these proofs in detail, showing the consistent pattern of argumentation.

Guided Path
1
List the five attributes
Read the passage and identify the five negative attributes: pre-eternity, everlastingness, self-subsistence, being unlike originated things, and oneness.
2
Analyze each proof
For each attribute, note the conditional: if it were absent, then something that entails huduth would follow. For example, without pre-eternity, huduth would be necessary.
The proofs are succinct; focus on the logical implication.
3
See the common pattern
All five proofs use the same template: absence of attribute leads to huduth, which is impossible, so attribute is necessary.
This reinforces the central thesis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ثم أشار الناظم تغمده المولى برحمته إلى برهان السلبية المتقدمة دليل الصفات بقوله: (لو لم يكن أي: إنما وجب اتصافه تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى بالصفات السلبية، لأنه لو لم يكن متصفا بها لزم حدوثه تعالى وتنزه عن. القدم فظاهر، إذ لا واسطة بين القدم والحدوث، فحيث انتفى الحدوث ثبت له القدم.
وأما البقاء، فلأنه لو لم يكن متصفّا بها لم يكن قديما، فإن من ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه.
وأما القيام بالنفس، فلأنه لو قام بغيره لكان عرضًا محتاجًا في قيامه للغير، وهو محال.
وأما المخالفة للحوادث، فلأنه لو ماثل شيئًا منها لكان حادثا مثلها.
وأما الوحدانية، فلأنه لو كان له نظير ومثيل في ذاته أو صفاته، للزم العجز، وكل عاجز حادث، كما أن كل حادث عاجز، والحدوث عليه محال، كما قال: (وهو) أي: الحدوث عليه تعالى (محال) لا يقبل الثبوت عقلا، (فاستقم) أي: اطلب من الله تعالى طريق الاستقامة، فإنها خير من ألف كرامة.
وإنما كان الحدوث عليه تعالى محالا.
لأنه يفضي) من أفضى يفضي، أي: يؤدي ويوصل إلى التسلسل)
التسلسل والدورا إذا استمر العدد إلى ما لا نهاية له، لأن التسلسل: هو ترتب أمور غير متناهية، وهو محال.
(والدور) أي: يفضي إلى الدور - بفتح الدال المشددة إن لم يستمر، لأن معنى الدور: توقف الشيء على ما يتوقف على ذلك الشيء من جهة واحدة، وهو محال كما قال: (وهو المستحيل المنجلي)، أي: الواضح الذي لا يحتاج إلى دليل.
If He were not described with them, His temporal origination (huduth) would follow, and it is impossible, so remain upright. | 28. Then the versifier, may the Lord envelop him in His mercy, indicated the aforementioned proof of the negative attributes—the proof of the attributes—by his saying: (If He were not described with them, i.e., it is only necessary that He, Blessed and Exalted, be described with the negative attributes, because if He were not described with them, His temporal origination (huduth) would be necessary, and by His exaltedness He is free from that. As for pre-eternity (qidam), it is obvious, for there is no intermediate between pre-eternity and temporal origination; so wherever temporal origination is negated, pre-eternity is affirmed for Him. As for everlastingness (baqa'), because if He were not described with it, He would not be pre-eternal; for whoever's pre-eternity is established, His non-existence is impossible. As for self-subsistence (qiyam bi nafsihi), because if He subsisted through another, He would be an accident (arad) needing another for His subsistence, which is impossible. As for being unlike originated things (mukhalafat al-hawadith), because if He resembled any of them, He would be originated like them. As for oneness (wahdaniyya), because if He had a peer or likeness in His essence or attributes, incapacity ('ajz) would follow, and every incapable being is originated, just as every originated being is incapable, and temporal origination is impossible for Him, as He said: (And it) i.e., temporal origination for Him, Exalted, (is impossible) not rationally acceptable, (so remain upright) i.e., ask Allah for the path of rectitude, for it is better than a thousand miracles. And temporal origination is only impossible for Him, Exalted, because it leads to infinite regress) from afda yufdi, i.e., leads and arrives at infinite regress (tasalsul) and circularity (dawr) if the number continues without end, for tasalsul is the arrangement of non-finite things, and it is impossible. (And dawr) i.e., it leads to dawr—with a fat-ha on the emphasized dal—if it does not continue, because the meaning of dawr is the dependence of something on that which depends on that same thing from one aspect, and it is impossible, as he said: (And it is the clear impossibility) i.e., the evident one that does not need proof.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessity of God's negative attributes. The versifier (Sanusi) states in line 28 that if God were not described with these attributes, then temporal origination (huduth) would follow, and huduth is impossible for God. The commentator explains each of the five negative attributes: pre-eternity (qidam), everlastingness (baqa'), self-subsistence (qiyam bi nafsihi), being unlike originated things (mukhalafat al-hawadith), and oneness (wahdaniyya). For each, he shows that the lack of the attribute would entail huduth, which is impossible. Then he explains why huduth is impossible: because it would lead to either infinite regress (tasalsul) or circularity (dawr), both of which are rationally impossible. The argument is that if God were originated, then His existence would be dependent on a prior cause, leading to an infinite chain (tasalsul) if that causal sequence extended endlessly, or to circular dependence (dawr) if the causal chain eventually looped back. Both are absurd. Thus, huduth is impossible for God, and therefore He must possess the negative attributes that negate any possibility of huduth.

Key Terms
سلوبية
قدم
بقاء
قيام بالنفس
مخالفة للحوادث
وحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the proof for oneness (wahdaniyya), what would follow if God had a peer?
A) Multiplicity in essence
B) Incapacity ('ajz)
C) Temporal origination directly
D) Need for a creator

Key Takeaway
Each negative attribute is proven individually by showing its absence entails huduth, which is impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is truly unlike anything you have ever seen or imagined, why do you still form mental images of Him when you try to focus in prayer? What would it take to purify your worship of even subtle anthropomorphism?
?
The proof shows that if God had a peer, He would be incapable. Do you ever rely on anything—money, status, people—as if it holds independent power alongside Him? What step can you take today to shift that reliance entirely to Him?
?
You affirm that God is self-subsistent and needs nothing, yet your anxieties about the future reveal a heart that seeks security in other things. How can the certainty of qiyam bi nafsihi transform your response to fear this week?

Why Huduth is Impossible: Tasalsul and Dawr
Sanusi proves impossibility of huduth through tasalsul and dawr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational arguments against the possibility of huduth for God, namely that it leads to tasalsul (infinite regress) or dawr (circularity), both of which are impossible.

Core Idea
Huduth is impossible because it would lead to infinite regress or circular dependency.

After establishing that the absence of negative attributes would entail huduth, Sanusi explains why huduth itself is impossible: it would either set off an infinite chain of causes (tasalsul) or a circular dependency (dawr). This lesson unpacks these two rational arguments, which are foundational in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of huduth's impossibility
Read the passage that begins with 'And temporal origination is only impossible for Him...' to understand the two arguments.
2
Understand tasalsul (infinite regress)
Tasalsul is an arrangement of non-finite things. If huduth were possible, the causal chain would continue without end, which is rationally impossible.
This argument shows that an infinite chain of causes is absurd.
3
Understand dawr (circularity)
Dawr is the dependence of something on that which depends on it. If the chain does not continue infinitely, it would loop, also impossible.
Circularity leads to logical contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ِلَوْ لَم يَكُنْ مُتَّصِفًا بِها لَزِمْ * حُدُوتُهُ وَهُوَ مُحالٌ فَاسْتَقِمْ | ۲۸
ثم أشار الناظم تغمده المولى برحمته إلى برهان السلبية المتقدمة دليل الصفات بقوله: (لو لم يكن أي: إنما وجب اتصافه تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى بالصفات السلبية، لأنه لو لم يكن متصفا بها لزم حدوثه تعالى وتنزه عن. القدم فظاهر، إذ لا واسطة بين القدم والحدوث، فحيث انتفى الحدوث ثبت له القدم.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that an infinite regress of causes is conceivable (e.g., the 'turtles all the way down' idea).
Correction: Theologians argue that an actual infinite regress is impossible because it would entail an infinite number of steps to reach the present, which cannot be traversed.

Checkpoint

A) Tasalsul and ta'til
B) Tasalsul and dawr
C) Dawr and tashbih
D) Ta'til and tashbih

Key Takeaway
Huduth leads to either tasalsul or dawr, both rationally impossible, so huduth is impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God were not eternal, could you truly rely on Him as unchanging? Examine your own heart: do you trust God as the eternal, uncaused Being, or unconsciously treat Him as one cause among others?
?
The argument against tasalsul shows that an infinite chain of causes is impossible. Look at your life: where have you been creating an infinite regress of excuses, or justifying sins by blaming previous circumstances? How can you break that chain today?
