Divine Attributes
intermediate
8 min
The Shahada Contains All Rulings
Commentator explains how all rulings are contained in the shahada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the two parts of the shahada—'Lā ilāha illa Allāh' and 'Muḥammad rasūl Allāh'—comprehensively encompass all Islamic doctrines: divine attributes, prophethood, and revealed matters.

Core Idea
The entire Islamic creed is contained in a single sentence: Lā ilāha illa Allāh, Muḥammad rasūl Allāh.

The commentator shows that the shahada is not just a formula but the summary of everything a Muslim believes. Each part implies a whole set of theological truths. Let's see how the first part entails Allah's attributes and the second entails prophethood and its requirements.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get its flow. Then read the translation. Notice how the commentator begins by stating that all rulings are contained in the word of Islam, then explains each part.
2
Identify the two parts of the shahada
The passage splits the shahada into two statements: 'Lā ilāha illa Allāh' (the first part) and 'Muḥammad rasūl Allāh' (the second part). Observe how each part is unpacked.
3
Understand the implications of the first part
The first part indicates that Allah is the Necessary Existent, Creator of the world. This entails attributes like power, will, knowledge, life, unity, creation, and negation of cause and nature. List these as you read.
The commentator says it implies 'all that was mentioned' from divine matters.
4
Understand the implications of the second part
The second part establishes prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). This entails his truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivering the message, intelligence, infallibility, and permissibility of human attributes that don't diminish his rank.
Notice the contrast: first part deals with Allah, second with the Prophet.
5
Reflect on why this matters
The Lawgiver accepted Islam only through this word. The passage shows that the shahada is comprehensive, making it the foundation of all Islamic teachings.
This underscores the importance of understanding the depth of the testimony of faith.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اندراج كل وينطوي) يَنْدَرج (في) معنى كلمة الإسلام) بكسر الكاف، ويَنْطَوِي فِي كِلْمَةِ الإِسْلام * ما قَدْ مَضَى مِنْ سَائِرِ الأَحْكَام وإسكان اللام، أي: الكلمة الدالة على الإسلام، وهي لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله (ما) قد مضى ذكره من سائر) أي: جميع (الأحكام) الإلهيات والنبويات والسمعيات، ولذلك اعتبر الشارع هذه الكلمة الجليلة للدخول في الإسلام وترجمة لما في القلب، ولم يقبل من أحد الإسلام إلا بها. وبيان ذلك ما قاله الناظم في شرحه»(۱) على سبيل الاختصار المفيد، وهو أن الله عَلم على الذات الواجب الوجود الخالق للعالم، وقد دلّت هذه الجملة على حصر الألوهية فيه تعالى، وظاهر أن ذلك يتضمن جميع ما ذكر، فإن وجوب الوجود يتضمن صفات السلوب ما عدا الوحدانية، والتنزه عن الأعراض في الأفعال والأحكام، وكونه خالقا للعالم يتضمن القدرة، والإرادة والعلم، والحياة، والوحدانية، وحدوث العالم بأسره (۲)، ونفي العلة، والطبيعة. وأما الجملة الثانية، وهو قولنا: (محمد رسول الله فقد دلت على ثبوت الرسالة لنبينا صلى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ، وذلك يستلزم صدقه في كل ما أخبر عنه، وأمانته، وتبليغه الرسالة للعباد، وكل ما أمر به، وفطانته، والرسول لا يكون إلا معصوما، واستحالة أضدادها عليه صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، وجواز كل ما لا يؤدي إلى نقص في علو مرتبته من الأعراض البشرية.
The inclusion of everything, and 'yanṭawī' (it is contained) in the meaning of the word of Islam (with kasr of the kāf and sukūn of the lām), i.e., the word that indicates Islam, and it is 'there is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' (what) has passed from the rest, i.e., all (of the rulings) of the divine matters, the prophetic matters, and the samʿī matters. Therefore, the Lawgiver considered this noble word for entering into Islam and as an expression of what is in the heart, and He did not accept from anyone Islam except with it. And the explanation of that is what the author said in his commentary (1) by way of useful brevity: that 'Allah' is a sign for the essence necessary of existence, the creator of the world. And this sentence indicated the restriction of divinity to Him, exalted. And it is apparent that that includes all that was mentioned: for the necessity of existence entails the attributes of negation except for unity, and being free from accidents in actions and rulings, and His being creator of the world entails power, will, knowledge, life, unity, the temporal origination of the entire world (2), and the negation of cause and nature. As for the second sentence, which is our statement: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', it indicates the establishment of prophethood for our Prophet (peace be upon him). And that entails his truthfulness in everything he informed about, his trustworthiness, his delivery of the message to the servants, everything he commanded, his intelligence, and the Prophet is not except as infallible, and the impossibility of their opposites for him (peace be upon him), and the permissibility of everything that does not lead to deficiency in the highness of his rank from human attributes.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage demonstrates how the entire corpus of Islamic teachings is contained within the two statements of the shahada (testimony of faith). The commentator first explains that the word 'Islam' refers to the declaration 'Lā ilāha illa Allāh, Muḥammad rasūl Allāh'. All divine (ilāhiyyāt), prophetic (nubuwwāt), and samʿī (revelational) rulings are included in this word. The Lawgiver made this word the sole criterion for entering Islam. The commentator then elaborates by summarizing the author's explanation. The first part ('Allāh') indicates the Necessary Existent, the Creator, and implies tawḥīd (divine unity) and all the attributes of negation (sifāt al-salūb) except for the attribute of unity itself. It also implies being free from accidents, and that God is the Creator entails power, will, knowledge, life, unity, the temporal origination of the world, and the negation of cause and nature. The second part ('Muḥammad rasūl Allāh') establishes prophethood and entails the Prophet's truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivery of the message, intelligence, infallibility, and the impossibility of their opposites. It also permits human attributes that do not diminish his rank.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the shahada is an empty formula without deep meaning.
Correction: The passage shows that the shahada comprehensively contains all Islamic doctrines, including divine attributes, prophethood, and revealed matters.

Checkpoint
What does the first part of the shahada ('Lā ilāha illa Allāh') entail according to the explanation?
A) Only that God exists, without any attributes.
B) The necessity of existence, attributes of negation, and that God is the Creator with attributes like power and will.
C) Only that Muhammad is a prophet.
D) That God has a body and is subject to change.

Key Takeaway
The shahada is the comprehensive foundation of all Islamic beliefs, encompassing divine attributes, prophethood, and revealed teachings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite the shahada daily, but have you ever reflected that by saying it you commit to acknowledging that every law and truth comes from Allah through His Prophet? How do your actions today reflect or betray this comprehensive commitment?
?
The passage teaches that the first part of the shahada implies that Allah is free from all imperfection and that He is the sole Creator. In what area of your life do you most often act as if something else—your habits, society, or your own desires—holds creative power over you?
?
If you truly believed that the Prophet is infallible in everything he conveyed, would you still find yourself picking and choosing which of his commands to follow? What would it take for you to submit fully to his sunnah, even when it contradicts your preferences?
